New Evidence Discovered in the Renhe Ship Disaster

Submission from the Tong, Ru, Chong, Hai, and Qi Five-County Association

A letter from the Shanghai Association of Natives of Tongzhou, Rugao, Chongming, Haian, and Qidong Counties to this newspaper states: "Regarding the case of the New Renhe steamer drowning and the theft of Ma Koubao and others, the news published in major newspapers at that time was based on information revealed by those claiming to be family members of the deceased. This association has received a report from Gu Jianan, the main witness in the case, sent by registered mail, along with two photos (showing the reward agreement signed by the family members of the deceased with him). After examining the contents, he deeply regrets being fooled by others and expresses his regret. The facts stated seem to be inconsistent with the news reported in various newspapers. We have also received multiple copies of printed lead type, with the same details as the original report and photos. In addition to keeping the original report on file, we are specially sending the printed report and two copies of the photos with this letter, requesting your newspaper to publish them in the news section so that the public can understand the truth and reveal the facts. We would be grateful for your cooperation."

Gu Jianan's Report: "To Whom It May Concern, in April of this year, the case of the New Renhe steamer murdering hawkers was reported in the newspapers for several days, causing a sensation in society for a time. Everyone believed that the reports in the newspapers were beyond doubt, and the court's conviction of the defendants only confirmed that the punishment was deserved. This matter has become a thing of the past. However, I never knew that human hearts are not what they used to be and that right and wrong are difficult to distinguish. The content is greatly different from what was reported in the newspapers. Jianan is a key witness in this case, and the conviction of the defendants was largely based on Jianan's testimony. In retrospect, I deeply regret my momentary foolishness in being instructed by others. Now, I can only announce the real situation so that the world can understand the truth and reduce my sins. On the evening of April 11th, members of the Yangtze River gang stole silver dollars from passengers. When they were discovered, they knocked out a passenger's front teeth. The next day, passengers were beaten by members of the Yangtze River gang. The sailors on the ship tried to mediate, but were stabbed with knives. This aroused the anger of the passengers, causing an uproar and chaos. It was heard that someone shouted that the perpetrators should be tied up. Jianan was on the ship selling beef for Zhang in the kitchen, so he was on the ship (there were no other hawkers on the ship) and learned of the above-mentioned disturbances. As for whether the perpetrators were tied up, I did not see it. On the 13th, the ship arrived in Shanghai, and Jianan immediately landed. The ship sailed away from Shanghai that day, and I did not go with the ship. On the 15th, Yu Shisheng, nicknamed Little Lion, the leader of the Yangtze River gang (this is the person who was arrested by the Water Police reported in the Shen Bao on September 2nd), came to my house two or three times, saying that there was a murder on the New Renhe ship, and accused me of being an accomplice. I told him that there was a fight on the ship at the time, but I did not hear of any murder, so how could I be an accomplice? He then said, 'What's the use of denying it? If you follow instructions, you will avoid being implicated and can make money.' I immediately refused and he left. The next day, Yu and Yang Chunting from the Water Police came with a pistol. Yang said, 'You didn't follow what Yu said yesterday, so I will arrest you and take you to the team to face charges. If you follow the instructions, we will organize an association of family members (the New Renhe disaster relief association reported in the newspapers), and each family will write a statement agreeing to give you one yuan a day, and in the future, we will take 20% of the compensation fee. We two will sign as guarantors,' and so on. At that time, I was threatened and lured with profit, and I was in a dilemma. If I did not agree, I would be immediately arrested and charged, and I could not predict the outcome. I asked Yang and Yu why they wanted to harm people for no reason. They replied, 'We don't want to put anyone to death for no reason. We're just using this to benefit everyone. Besides, when the money is in hand, we can settle the matter and not harm anyone. Why wouldn't you want to do it?' I asked how much the compensation fee would be. They said, 'You don't have to worry about this. We will find people to organize it. The more family members there are, the more compensation there will be.' Jianan believed them to be true at the time and agreed to do so. On the 18th, Yang brought Zhou Mengshi and others, saying that they had organized five family members, and each person could get at least 10,000 yuan in compensation, totaling 50,000 yuan. You have the hope of getting 10,000 yuan.' Yang Chunting took out a piece of paper from his sleeve, wrote a statement, and told me to keep it safe. He then ordered me to go to the Water Patrol Team to report the case and asked me to clearly recognize the faces of Zhou Mengshi and the other five people. In the evening, the Water Patrol Team set off to the New Renhe ship to Shanghai and arrested the people on board. When the entire staff was arrested and interrogated, Yang ordered me to listen to the interrogation and identify each person to ensure that I would not make a mistake when testifying in court. When I saw the crew members being tied up one by one and forced to confess, I felt like I was dreaming. There was no sign of the so-called money settlement, and many people were harmed. This was not what I originally expected. When my father found out about it, he severely reprimanded me. I reflected on it in the quiet of the night and regretted it too late. But the matter has come to this point, and there is nothing I can do. Now, I am stating the facts as they are. In addition to having already filed a statement with the court, I am attaching two photos of the statement made by Zhou Mengshi and others. I sincerely request your association to publish the above information in the newspapers so that the public can understand the truth and perhaps reduce my sins in the slightest. I hope for your public review. Respectfully submitted to the President of the Tong, Ru, Chong, Hai, and Qi Five-County Association, Gu Jianan (fingerprint), father writing on behalf of."

Statement by Zhou Mengshi and others: "Because our husbands and others were brutally murdered, please ask the authorities to redress the injustice. We request that Gu Jianan, an eyewitness, provide evidence. Fearing that it will hinder daily business, we are willing to pay back one yuan per day for the loss. If we receive compensation in the future, we are willing to offer 20% of the total amount as a reward. Fearing that words are not enough to rely on, we are making this statement as evidence. Late evening of April 18, 22nd year of the Republic of China. Zhou Mengshi (signed), Mei Yu (signed), Ma Chen (signed), Sun Zhang (signed), Wei Zhu (signed), Yu Baosheng (signed), Yang Chunting (signed), Gu (held), Witness."

Strange News of a Poor Man Selling Himself

A Husband Can Be Obtained for £60

New Jersey, Camden, USA. It is common for women to sell themselves to find husbands due to poverty, but it has never been heard of for men to sell themselves to find wives due to poverty. A local newspaper here recently carried an advertisement that reads: "Unemployed man Mr. Haines, 25 years old, widowed, with a son of just three years old, who is very lovable. Now, due to maternal hardship, if any decent and honest person can offer £60 to help him, he is willing to devote himself to them and guarantees to be a good partner." (Reuters) Brothers, I will take the meaning of 崇實 Saving the Nation as the topic of today's speech. I hope that all the people of the country will commemorate this serious national crisis with the spirit of 崇實 and save our precarious national destiny. Regarding the meaning of 崇實, since the national crisis, whether I am giving a speech anywhere or writing articles for any newspaper, I have almost always directly or indirectly paid attention to this point. I remember that when I gave a radio broadcast speech this spring, I said something like this: The greatest danger in China now lies in the fact that the general public still does not know the true meaning of the national crisis, nor the reasons for the national crisis. Those who lead the public to save the nation only engage in superficial excitement and do not make practical efforts. Therefore, although there has been a national salvation movement after every national crisis in the past century, every national salvation movement has ultimately failed to save China. Our enlightened people should learn from the pain, and from now on, thoroughly understand the meaning of the national crisis, reflect on the causes of the national crisis, be down-to-earth, and make a firm and courageous determination to fight and save the nation. We must encourage ourselves with perseverance and make practical efforts in terms of culture, education, the duties of our respective professions, and our usual lifestyles, so as to enrich the content of national life and consolidate the foundation for national development. Every bit of effort we make is a bit of salvation for the country, and the sum of the efforts of the people of the whole country is the final success of the nation's efforts to wipe out its humiliation and become strong. Our Chinese nation was originally one of the first nations in the world to create culture. The reason why the Chinese nation was able to create culture first was because our ancestors worked hard and devoted themselves to improving their lives or the environment. Unfortunately, this spirit of creating culture, 崇實, and striving gradually disappeared after the Han Dynasty. By the time of the Jin, Wei, and Six Dynasties, the fatuous emperors, treacherous ministers, aristocratic rich, defeated generals, remnants of soldiers, palace women, official prostitutes, and men of letters abandoned the inherent spirit of creating culture of our nation, indulged in debauchery, and were obsessed with money and pleasure. They were completely unable to recognize their responsibilities to the country and society, and even had no purpose in their personal lives. For thousands of years, the spirit of education has been to cultivate emotions, and the only desire of the intellectual class is to prepare for laziness. The so-called "ten years of hard study" is nothing more than a plan for lifelong comfort. Although education has been reformed in recent years, a boatload of Confucian scholars still dream of Western-style houses, cars, beautiful clothes, and abundant food, all kinds of tools and equipment for laziness and comfort. As for the practical problems of the general public's clothing, food, housing, and transportation, how they should be improved and how they should be solved, they are completely ignored and completely irresponsible, and their own needs in life must be relied upon by others. Because of the laziness, vanity, and parasitism of the scholar-officials, Chinese society has caused national education to be unrelated to the people's lives and the survival of the nation, and has no benefit whatsoever. The whole country, from top to bottom, is moving towards this dead end of selfishness, greed, laziness, and indulgence. No one is willing to fulfill their practical responsibility of labor and production for the nation and the country. There are few who produce and many who consume, so how can the people's livelihood not be tight, the country not be poor, and the nation not be weak? Therefore, the only urgent task for us to save the country today is to restore the inherent spirit of creating culture of our nation, be down-to-earth, and work hard to increase national production and improve the lives of the people. If a nation cannot be independent culturally or economically and must rely on foreigners in everything, it is the greatest danger and the greatest shame for a nation. Therefore, since ancient times, the principle of national rejuvenation has always been to focus on 生聚 and 教訓. In ancient times when science and culture were immature, it still required ten years of 生聚 and ten years of 教訓 in order to seek rejuvenation. Today, when science and culture are advancing by leaps and bounds, if we do not fundamentally restore the ability of our nation to create culture, and do not work hard and encourage ourselves with perseverance and practical efforts to enrich the content of national survival and consolidate the foundation for national development, but only talk about resisting the enemy and empty talk about saving the nation, then it only shows the immaturity and vanity of the national psychology, and the effort to save the nation and become strong will never have the slightest practical effect. Soviet Russian Aid Association Manager Accused

Plaintiff Sues for Illegal Infringement of Freedom and Other Crimes

The Second Trial Was Held Yesterday, and the Defendants Were Released on Bail

Mikev, a Russian manager of the Soviet Russian Aid Association at No. 2 Beijing Road, previously filed a case in the First Special District Court against a Russian named Morrison for embezzlement. Judge Qian has already ruled that Morrison is not guilty. Now, Morrison has also hired lawyer Qiu Fenling to sue Mikev, the manager of the Soviet Union Aid Association, Russian deputy manager Bobiqu, bookkeeper Kraslafsky, staff Yazimengaou, female secretary Maoxifa, and Russian woman Biegaofa, and six other people, at the First Special District Court, for illegally arresting, detaining, robbing property, and fabricating false accusations. The reasons for the prosecution are roughly as follows: The plaintiff, Morrison, used to be an employee of the first defendant, Mikev's company, for many years and has never made any mistakes. In May of this year, Mikev, because the plaintiff was unwilling to help him with political work, wanted to send Mao back to Soviet Russia for punishment. Mao, fearing misfortune, had no choice but to avoid Hankou. Mikev, angered out of shame, falsely accused him of embezzlement and filed a criminal lawsuit. At the same time, the fourth, fifth, sixth, and third defendants were sent to break into Morrison's residence at No. 374 Jiangxi Road with weapons, imprisoning Mao's wife in the bathroom, ransacking boxes and cabinets, and robbing him of 11,177 US dollars in cash, 722 British pounds, a bank passbook, and a check. Defendants two and three issued receipts. Afterwards, Mao returned to Shanghai to respond to the lawsuit and was declared not guilty. Although Mao only asked Mikev to return the lost items, he admitted that he had handed over the bank passbook and check to the Far East Bank, but completely denied the huge amount of cash. Since Mikev has already admitted that the passbook and other items were handed over to the Far East Bank, it is undeniable that they were robbed from the plaintiff. It is found that Mikev first fabricated false accusations and illegally infringed on the freedom of others, and then robbed others of their property. He has committed crimes under Articles 180, 316, and 341 of the Criminal Law. The actions of the other defendants in jointly carrying out the crime have also constituted a crime and should be investigated and punished according to the law, and ordered to pay compensation, etc. The court, according to the complaint, summoned the defendants on September 7th and ordered the case to be retried at 11:00 a.m. on the 18th. If a certain defendant did not appear, lawyer Wei would be responsible, and the deposit of 5,000 yuan would be confiscated according to law. The defendant must also be taken into custody for interrogation. Yesterday morning at 11:00 a.m., the date for the trial of this case had arrived. Judge Xue Lanru presided over the trial in the Eighth Criminal Court. Because this case was of great importance, many Russian men and women and reporters from various Western newspapers came to court to listen. All six defendants also appeared in court and hired lawyers Chen Yingzhang, Shi Zhao, Zou Lianfeng, Li Zuyu, and Wei to defend them. Judge Xue first interrogated the plaintiff, Morrison, and after he made his statement, he interrogated each defendant one by one until 2:00 p.m., when the interrogation was still not completed. The official then ordered the case to be retried next Thursday, and the defendants were still released on bail after paying the original bail.

Closing Arguments in the Suspected Murder of Wife Case

丨Sentencing Scheduled for the 25th丨

A case of suspected murder of a wife occurred in the Bu family's house in Caijia Lane, Yangjing, Pudong, causing a sensation in the surrounding area. The husband's aunt, Jiang Gu Shi, and the husband, Jiang A'gen, have been prosecuted by the local court. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 p.m., Judge Yang Qianchang continued the trial. The defendant hired lawyer Xue Jiesheng to defend him. The official asked Jiang Gu Shi, who stated that she was 41 years old, a native of Shanghai, and lived at No. 26 Duanjia Lane, Yangjing, Pudong. Jiang A'gen is my son. I gave birth to him when I was 19 years old. My husband's name is Jiang Sihai, and he is dead. Jiang Zhu Shi is my daughter-in-law. Q: When did you marry her? A: On the second day of the tenth month of the year before last. Q: Are you and your daughter-in-law usually on good terms? A: Yes. Q: Do you live with your son and daughter-in-law? A: Yes, we lived together. Later, we moved out on October 24th. Q: Did you move to a new house? A: Yes, my daughter-in-law and son moved to the old house. Q: Did your daughter-in-law and son quarrel on April 9th this year? A: No. Q: How did your daughter-in-law die? A: She went out to pick vegetables and I don't know how she died in the river. Q: There are injuries on her head, which were found to have been caused by a hoe. Where did they come from? A: I don't know. Q: Blood stains and a bloody vegetable were found in the vegetable garden of your new house. The test results show that it is the same as your daughter-in-law's blood. A: This was because her mother's family destroyed my house. The children were watching the fun and broke the glass, and the blood dripped on the ground. Q: There are stab wounds on the top of your daughter-in-law's head. A: When my son went to see the body, there were no injuries. Q: After your son fought with your daughter-in-law, maybe she committed suicide. A: There have never been any quarrels. Q: The prosecutor's indictment states that your son injured her and she died in the river. A: It's a false accusation. At this point, the official asked Jiang A'gen, who stated that he was 23 years old, a native of Shanghai. Jiang Gu Shi is my mother, and Jiang Zhu Shi is my wife, whom I married in October of the 20th year of the Republic of China. Q: Are your wife and mother on good terms? A: We have always been on good terms. Q: Why did you separate? A: Because she didn't wash the clothes cleanly, I slightly admonished her and she asked to separate. Q: Did you fight with your wife on April 9th? A: We never quarrel. Q: There are injuries on her head and waist. A: When I went to see the body, there were no injuries at all. Later, I went to call my mother out, and they beat me. I don't know how the injuries happened afterwards. He then cried loudly. The official asked the plaintiff, Zhu Zhao Shi, who stated that she was 58 years old, a native of Shanghai, and lived in Yangjing. The deceased, Jiang Zhu Shi, is my daughter, and Jiang A'gen is my son-in-law. My daughter is 24 years old this year and married at the age of 22. They often fight and cry when they come back. We always send her back and say good things to them. This time, she was brutally murdered by them, which is the truth, but I did not witness it. Her son, Zhu Guisheng, stated that he was 36 years old, the deceased was his younger sister, and his words were the same as his mother's. The official said that it is possible for husband and wife to fight and injure each other, but it is unlikely that she would be thrown into the river. Perhaps she committed suicide out of anger. He then asked the witness, Zhu Minghai, who stated that he was 27 years old, lived in the same house as Zhu Guisheng, and did not know about everything about this case because he was working in Puxi. At this point, Prosecutor Li presented his opinion, and then lawyer Xue Jiesheng stood up to defend, saying that the crime in this case is called murder, which is very broad in criminal law. There must be all kinds of acts of murder, and there must be concrete acts of murder. The court must protect human rights and seek justice for the victims, which is the duty of national law. However, the defendants are the victim's mother-in-law, husband and wife, and close relatives. Now, only relying on the statements of Zhu Zhao Shi and others is just empty talk. The examination has raised doubts. At the same time, the atmosphere in the market villages is not open. After this incident, rumors spread, causing a sensation in the city, and it was assumed that someone had committed the crime of murder. However, the act and the result of the law must have material evidence, oral evidence, and circumstantial evidence, which are completely lacking now, and it is inevitable that the facts are fabricated. Seeing that the plaintiff destroyed the house, he knew that he could not determine that his daughter was murdered. As for the blood on the vegetables, it is said to be the same. However, Shanghai doctors must choose the same blood type when transfusing blood, so the blood type cannot constitute evidence of a crime. Moreover, a man in the countryside spends thousands of gold to marry a woman, would he be willing to put her to death for no reason, not fearing that it would hinder the ancestral rites? Therefore, this case, based on the analysis of no evidence, should be found not guilty. At this point, the official announced the end of the arguments and announced that the verdict would be announced on the afternoon of the 25th. The defendant was sent back to custody.

Foreign Soldier Forcibly Drove a Car Causing an Accident

Beating a Chauffeur and Killing Xu Shui Jin

Fled Without a Trace Afterwards, Police Investigating Strictly

Yesterday's Autopsy, the Foreign Soldier Still Not Apprehended

A foreign national wearing a military uniform of a certain country suddenly came to the Hua'an Automobile Company at No. 27 Tiantong Road on the morning before yesterday and rented a car with the number 17838, saying that he wanted to go to Zhao Feng Park. At that time, the fare was agreed upon as $1.50, and the chauffeur Li Mao Di was driving. Unexpectedly, when the car drove to the west of Hart Road, the foreign national forcibly seized the chauffeur's position and drove the car himself. Li refused, and was beaten by the foreign national with fists and feet. He was eventually overpowered. When the car had barely reached Yu Yuan Road, near Di Feng Road, it carelessly knocked down a local resident, Xu Shui Jin, 27 years old, and the rickshaw he was riding, with both man and vehicle falling to the ground. Xu was severely injured by the car running over him. Seeing that he had caused an accident, the foreign national quickly jumped out of the car and fled westward. Li was extremely shocked at this sight, and immediately gave chase behind the car, but it was too late and the foreign national escaped. Afterwards, a Chinese constable No. 1569 happened to see this and immediately notified the Jing'an Temple Police Station by telephone, ordering detective Qian Xianzhang to go to investigate. He then sent the injured person to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and he died shortly thereafter. The body was taken to the autopsy station on Bian Lun Road. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court dispatched Prosecutor Guo Wei to the station to examine the body. The case was opened and Li Mao Di testified that the foreign national came to rent a car that day, and his accent was like English. He was wearing a military uniform. The company assigned me as the driver, but unexpectedly, when we got to Hart Road, he wanted to drive himself. Because my duties were at stake, I firmly refused. He then used violent means to beat me, causing injuries to my head. I was weak and unable to resist, and he was eventually overpowered and drove away. Not long after driving, this accident happened. Chinese constable No. 1569 also testified that at the time the car knocked down the person, he didn't witness it. He only saw a foreign soldier running madly westward, and the chauffeur was chasing after him. He also saw the deceased being crushed by the car and falling to the ground, unconscious. I then reported it to the police station. After obtaining the statements, Mr. Guo ordered that Xu Shui Jin, the deceased, was indeed crushed and killed by car number 17838 before his death. The foreign national who caused the accident is being strictly investigated by the police station according to the law. The body was handed over to his wife, Xu Wu Shi, after she made a statement, to be returned for burial.

Road Administration Inspection Team's Report on the Inspection of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway

Points out areas for improvement in train operation and stations.

The Railway Bureau ordered relevant departments to implement accordingly.

The Road Administration Inspection Team of the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, led by Director Huang Boqiao, inspected the model stations along the Beijing-Shanghai Railway for the first time on the 6th of this month and has already returned to Shanghai. The inspection process and opinions have been reported, and after research by the Railway Bureau, instructions have been issued to the relevant departments to implement them separately. The report is as follows:

Train Operation

The trains were generally in good condition, but the following points should still be noted: (1) If passengers take up multiple seats with their luggage or obstruct other passengers' seats, the passenger transport inspectors and ticket collectors should inform them politely. If necessary, they can arrange for someone to help place the luggage on the luggage rack. (2) All old glass mirrors, old regulations, and other dirty door fittings on the train should be removed. (3) Absolutely prohibit fare evasion. (4) If any unusual or abnormal conditions are found during train operation, the train personnel should immediately notify the driver to pay attention. (5) The practice of using a side track for train exchange at the Benniu Station is inappropriate and should be investigated and reported.

Major Stations

(1) Suzhou Station: (a) The space is small, crowded, and disorderly, and the food sold is also unhygienic and should be strictly prohibited. (b) The interior and exterior of the station and the kitchen of the dining hall are unclean and should be rectified within a time limit. (c) The wiring throughout the station is messy and should be rectified immediately. (d) Rickshaw pullers outside the station shout and push when trains arrive and passengers exit the station, obstructing passengers. The local public security bureau should be consulted to find a way to quickly ban this. (2) Wuxi Station: (a) The information desk should be improved immediately. It should not be located inside the platform but in the station hall. (b) Notice boards should be placed in appropriate locations so that passengers can easily read them. (c) The noise from vehicles outside the station is the same as in Suzhou. (3) Changzhou Station: (a) The interior and exterior of the station are unusually messy, and the walls of the waiting room and station building are particularly unclean. (b) The information desk is the same as in Wuxi and should be improved immediately. (4) Zhenjiang Station: The overall order of the station is well-maintained and relatively clean and should be commended.

Welcoming the Anti-Japanese Heroes' Association Delegation to Suzhou to Present a Banner to Su Bingwen

To be held at the Garden Hotel at 12:00 noon today

The Shanghai Municipal Organizations' Welcoming Committee for Anti-Japanese Hero General Ma Su's Return to China previously selected Ye Jiaxing, Sun Mingqi, Wang Honghui, Chen Binghui, Wang Hesong, and others as representatives to present a banner. Sun Mingqi and others departed for Suzhou yesterday and agreed with General Su Bingwen to hold the banner presentation ceremony at 12:00 noon on the 19th at the auditorium of the Suzhou Garden Hotel. Housing for Troops of Wang and Li - Postal Savings Bureau Approves a 10% Rent Reduction

Reply has been sent to charitable organizations in Shanghai.

The Shanghai Charitable Organizations United Relief Association for Northeastern Refugees previously housed over 130 family members of the anti-Japanese generals Wang Delin and Li Du's troops. The Association leased four buildings, numbers 16, 17, 18, and 25, in the Laishou Lane on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession from the Shanghai Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau Business Department, at a total monthly rent of 426 yuan. The Association requested the Bureau to reduce the monthly rent to save expenses, as raising funds was difficult and the refugees could not be sent back for the time being. It is now learned that the Association has received a reply, temporarily approving a 10% rent reduction.

Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to Municipal Council Requesting Restoration of the Old System of Taxing Pawnshops

Businesses are slow and unable to bear heavy taxes.

Hope that the Municipal Council does not kill the goose that lays the golden egg in order to maintain tax revenue.

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Municipal Council yesterday, stating that the pawnbroking industry is heavily taxed and unable to bear the burden, requesting the restoration of the old tax rate. The letter stated: "Regarding the case of the pawnbroking industry requesting the restoration of the old system of taxing 2/1000 of the pawned amount, we sent a letter to your bureau on July 15th along with a survey form, but have not yet received a reply. Now, we have received a letter from the Shanghai Pawnbroking Industry Association, stating that members in the Public Concession are suffering from declining business and request the Municipal Council to continue taxing 2/1000 of the pawned amount in accordance with the original regulations to maintain their businesses. The Association had previously compared the actual business volume of each firm over the past three years with the current tax payments and prepared a survey form to be forwarded to the Municipal Council as proof. It is now reported that all members within the Concession have stated that business has become increasingly slow and they are unable to pay the huge taxes. Therefore, they unanimously request that starting from this winter, the Municipal Council should offset the overpaid tax of 9,348 yuan from the previous three years and the overpaid tax of 1,442 yuan from this summer. If this is not done, they fear they will be unable to maintain their businesses and will follow in the footsteps of Yuan Tianchang Hongsheng and other pawnshops by suspending operations. They also reported the pawned amount and tax paid for this summer, requesting that we prepare a form and send it to the Municipal Council for verification. After investigation, the above statements are true and accurate. Therefore, we are sending the newly prepared survey form in duplicate to your bureau for review and request that you also forward the plea of our members to the Municipal Council for approval. We hope that you will consider restoring the good system as soon as possible to avoid killing the goose that lays the golden egg and to maintain tax revenue.

Zhejiang Public Association Continues to Request Suspension of Land Survey and Mapping Fees

The Zhejiang Public Association continues to petition the Zhejiang Provincial Government, requesting the immediate suspension of land survey and mapping fees. To Chairman Lu of the Zhejiang Provincial Government: In our previous telegram, we requested changes to the land survey methods and a reduction in expenses. We received a reply stating that the request had been forwarded to the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Finance for consideration. We are grateful for your consideration. Large-scale surveys are costly. The survey in Hangzhou County has been ongoing for four or five years, costing over 2 million yuan, and has not yet been completed. Based on this, the land survey expenses for the entire province of 75 counties, large and small, will be over 50 or 60 million yuan. In this time of poverty and economic collapse, where will such a large amount of funds come from? Even with forced extortion, collecting a fee of 5 jiao per mu will likely fall far short of this amount, and it will be difficult to avoid abandonment halfway. After our telegram was published in newspapers, people from all walks of life sent letters suggesting triangulation or plane table surveying. They all agreed that the cost was too high and the people could not afford it. We plan to collect opinions from people throughout the province in the shortest possible time, concentrate on a suitable method, and submit it to your office for consideration by the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Finance. Before the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Finance submit their reply, we request that you order Haining, Jiaxing, Haiyan, Pinghu, Wuxing, Changxing, Qianshan, and Yuyao counties to immediately suspend the collection of survey and mapping fees to avoid waste and to relieve the burden on the people. Land consolidation is a necessary procedure for realizing land policy, and the people are eager for its implementation. However, we fear that it will be suspended due to financial constraints, repeating the mistakes of Hangzhou County and Shangshan Dongxiang. The people will bear the cost of the land survey but will not receive the benefits. This is not your original intention to govern with diligence. This matter concerns the interests of the entire province, and we dare not hesitate to appeal again and again.

Cleaning Workers' Strike in the Yinxiang District - Strike Started Yesterday Morning and Resumed in the Afternoon

The cleaning workers in the Yinxiang District demanded improved treatment and made conditions, which were rejected by the cleaning company. All workers went on strike yesterday morning, stopping the emptying of garbage buckets, which caused inconvenience to residents. Fortunately, after the mediation of Party and government organs, a resolution was reached, and work resumed completely at 3:00 p.m. yesterday. The details are as follows:

Strike Yesterday Morning

The Cleaning Industry Union of the Seventh District, at the request of its members, presented conditions for improved treatment to the cleaning company contracted in the Yinxiang District. Because the cleaning company had no sincerity in accepting, the mediation of the Fourth District Party Headquarters was ineffective. The union members, at a general meeting, resolved to organize a strike committee and scheduled the strike for the 17th. The strike was temporarily postponed after the advice of Party and government organs. However, the cleaning company insisted on not accepting the conditions. Therefore, all workers went on strike at 4:00 a.m. yesterday, stopping pushing carts and emptying garbage buckets. Residents in the Hongkou area felt quite inconvenienced. After the Fifth Precinct of the Public Security Bureau received the report, it immediately dispatched police to prevent incidents. All the striking workers lived at home. Fortunately, no incidents occurred.

Party and Government Advice

After receiving the report, the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau, considering that the cleaning workers' strike concerned public health, sent Lu Yinchu and Zhu Jintao to advise and mediate. They summoned Tang Jingshou of the cleaning company, Wang Asan of the Cleaning Industry Union of the Seventh District, Shen Ding of the Fourth District Party Headquarters, and Zhang Peishen, a gentleman from the Yinxiang District, to conduct mediation. Around 2:00 p.m., the cleaning company and the Shanghai Cleaning Workers' Union agreed to a resolution. All workers accepted the union's order to resume work at 3:00 p.m. yesterday.

Resolution

The resolution reached through mediation is as follows: (1) Wages will be increased by 25% across the board, starting from September 21st. (2) The cents in wages should be paid in silver dollars. (3) The cleaning company will subsidize each worker with 1 jiao and 5 fen silver dollars per day during rainy hours. (4) The cleaning company will issue 2 silver dollars per year to each worker for the purchase of cleaning equipment. (5) The cleaning company will subsidize the union's operational expenses with 40 silver dollars per month. (6) When hiring new workers in the future, union members should be given priority. (7) These conditions are valid until June of the 23rd year of the Republic.

Feng Laosi Released Yesterday

Garrison Headquarters Declares No Further Detention

Feng Laosi, a native of Shandong, was previously detained by Inspector Jiang Feng of the Huizi Police Station on suspicion of selling opium and handed over to the First Special District Local Court, requesting permission for continued detention. The court ordered Feng to provide a guarantor and leave the courtroom to await further questioning. Subsequently, the police station found that Feng was not involved, so Judge Wu ordered the cancellation of Feng's guarantee. Later, the Songhu Garrison Headquarters discovered that Feng Laosi was suspected of committing murder in the interior and sent personnel to request his transfer. Feng was therefore detained, pending the Garrison Headquarters presenting sufficient evidence for verification. These details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning was the date for the continued hearing of this case. Judge Xue Lanru ascended to the bench in the Eighth Criminal Court. The Garrison Headquarters also sent an official letter stating that Feng Laosi was not involved in the murder and declared no intention to transfer him. Lawyer Feng Yanfan argued in court that since Feng was not involved in the murder case, he should be released immediately. Judge Xue then ordered Feng Laosi's release.

New Ruiping Steamer Robbed

Robbers disguised as Coolies boarded as Passengers

Searching and Robbing Money and Clothes

Since the Yu Gu steamer robbery, there is still a group of pirates hiding in the Shanghai area, plotting to rob merchant ships. Various shipping companies in Shanghai were notified in advance and have been taking strict precautions. Passengers without guarantees are not allowed to board. This matter has been reported in this newspaper. The pirates, seeing the shipping companies taking such strict precautions, were unable to strike. Unexpectedly, they sneaked into Wenzhou inland and robbed merchant ships along the Zhejiang coast, making the shipping companies unable to defend themselves. The New Ruiping, a regular ship on the Ruian-Pingyang route in Wenzhou, belongs to the Shanghai Huxing Company. It operates between Shanghai and Ruiping and has excellent business. There are four ships operating on the same route. The New Ruiping left Ruian on Monday, stopping at various small ports along the way to Shanghai. On Tuesday morning, the ship arrived at Chumen and stopped to load cargo and passengers as usual. Unexpectedly, nine pirates, each carrying a handgun, disguised as coolies and boarded the ship. There were no inspecting soldiers or police in the area, so the pirates were able to board the ship safely. Not long after the New Ruiping set sail, at around 8:40 a.m., the pirates on board split into groups and started robbing. It was said that when the pirates started robbing, they first pretended to fight. Then, two of the pirates, armed with guns, coerced and monitored the captain, driver, and accountant. The remaining pirates searched the passengers' cabins, first robbing money, then clothes, and then miscellaneous items. Even silver coins and copper coins were robbed. For twelve hours, the New Ruiping was controlled by the pirates and had to listen to their commands. It was not until 9:00 p.m., when the ship arrived near Haimen, that the pirates released a sampan into the sea and forced two fishing boats nearby to transport the stolen goods ashore before escaping. The total loss is estimated to be nearly 10,000 yuan. Some passengers who resisted the pirates were shot and injured, but their lives are not in danger. When the pirates were robbing, several barges at the Chumen pier heard gunshots and then cries coming from the New Ruiping. The boatmen on the barges reported this to the branch office, but because the ship had no radio and no marine police, there was no way to help. After the pirates had finished looting and escaped, the ship returned to Shanghai. The Huxing Company gave each of the affected passengers a relief fund of 15 yuan. The company has now reported the incident to the military and police authorities in Ruiping, requesting them to quickly arrest the pirates. They are also discussing anti-theft and safe navigation measures with other shipping companies on the same route.

Spring and Autumn

His Talent Is Not As Good As You, Your Life Is Not As Good As Him

— Jun Ti

Zhu Yuanzhang, while at the Huangjue Temple, suddenly had worldly desires and was unwilling to continue accompanying the green lamp and ancient Buddha. He took up his spear and broadsword, and fought his way out of Haozhou. When he established his capital in Nanjing, he was overjoyed and said to his subordinates, "Unexpectedly, what started as a game has become reality!" One can imagine his elated state. Because he was too eager to govern, he often gave excessive rewards and punishments, which led to the following story circulating among the people.

It is said that once, after drinking a bit too much wine, he woke up from a nap and wanted some tea. Coincidentally, a eunuch who was neither fully male nor fully female, brought him a bowl of strong tea. He was extremely pleased and bestowed countless rewards. A poor scholar learned of this and wrote two lines of poetry: "Ten years under a cold window, how does it compare to a cup of tea?" As he repeatedly recited the poem, Zhu Taizu happened to be passing by incognito. He knew it was a satire of him, so he continued the verse from outside: "His talent is not as good as you, your life is not as good as him!"

Wonderful! The philosophies of serving as an official and becoming wealthy, and the emperor's strategies for employing and administering people for thousands of years in China were revealed by these two lines of poetry. In reality, being an official does not necessarily require great talent, as long as one has good fortune, even without talent it is possible; having talent does not guarantee a high position, if one has a hard life, even great talent is useless. Officialdom and fate are interdependent, but have nothing to do with talent.

However, although Zhu Taizu valued fate over talent, he still employed grand masters to examine the scholar's eight-legged essay, rather than employing fortune tellers to arrange the scholar's birth chart. This can be considered as distinguishing true talent and dispelling superstition. In reality, it was still deception. This is called entrusting fate to talent, because those with good fate can succeed in all three imperial examinations even without talent, while those with bad fate will still have a miserable life. Acceptance or rejection still depends on fate and not on talent. Someone asked me, "Does China still value fate or talent more now?" I cannot answer. But among the gentlemen not in office, if they consider themselves to have great talent, then it is valuing fate; if they consider themselves useless, then it is valuing talent.

There is a way to remedy everything in the world. If talent is lacking, then put in ten years of effort under a cold window; if that is not enough, twenty years of effort; if that is still not enough, thirty years of effort will eventually do the trick. Only fate, once destined, cannot be changed. This humble one has spent days and nights racking my brains to come up with a half-baked solution that everyone might as well try.

This method is to ask men and women from all walks of life to first find a lucky day and time before starting to work at the grassroots level. This will align with the auspicious couplet: "Erecting pillars on an auspicious day; the beam raising meets the Purple Star." The offspring will surely be wealthy and noble. This can be predicted.

Locks and Keys

— Xian Xian

I recently installed a door lock, which inevitably led me to think about keys.

The Chinese do not pay much attention to locks. Is it because the Chinese have the virtues of not closing their doors at night and not picking up lost items on the road, or is it because bandits are rampant and locks are useless? Therefore, they casually put a lock on the door that can be opened with a piece of lead wire, and casually install a lock on the silver cabinet that can be opened with a lighter flint.

However, foreigners are different. They pay special attention to locks. Even if it is the same brand of lock, each one has its own unique structure. Therefore, each lock has a different key. Not to mention that a key from one brand cannot open a lock from another brand. Even a key for number 100 of a lock cannot open number 101 of the same lock.

Because of the relationship between locks and keys, I thought of the division in Chinese and Western academia.

Chinese people, after mastering the Four Books and Five Classics, and writing successful examination essays, can do anything after being placed on the gold list. Legislation, judiciary, administration, everything can be done. Moreover, after serving as a governor, they can then manage river works. If barbarians happen to revolt, they can immediately be appointed as commander-in-chief to suppress them. After serving as an imperial censor, they can be transferred to the Ministry of Revenue. If they are in the mood, they can even serve as a governor-general or train an army. This symbolizes that the keys to Chinese locks can open any lock.

If foreigners study a certain field, they cannot change careers for life. Their doctors cannot practice medicine if they do not come from medical school, unlike us who have scholar-physicians. They must have a law degree to practice law, unlike us who have Shaoxing legal secretaries. This symbolizes that locks have their own keys. Moreover, even if they are from the same engineering field, those who study electrical engineering will work in electrical engineering for life, and those who study railways will work in railways for life. This is the reason why a key for number 100 cannot open a lock for number 101.

In recent years, China has sent many students to study abroad, hoping to transform the old Chinese locks and keys into Western-style ones. However, to their surprise, those who studied literature, law, or agriculture can become police chiefs, water conservancy bureau chiefs, or county magistrates upon their return. There are many such examples. I have no name for these talents and can only call them Chinese-style Western locks.

The Art of Begging

— Wang Zhuyu

At the foot of the Xin Zha Bridge, a Russian was speaking to a Chinese beggar as if giving a lecture: "When you beg for money, you always hunch over with your head down and your back bent, without any spirited performance. Look at how we Russians beg for coins. We always stick our bellies out high and act respectfully and politely, first performing a full salute, and then opening our mouths to speak. Although our transaction is small, it should have some artistry. Otherwise, wouldn't the donor's money be wasted? Friends, remember! Times have evolved, and everything must have artistry. Begging is no exception, otherwise, you will fall behind!" Alas! In this day and age, begging really requires artistry.

Four Battalion Commanders of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Fifteen: Guests Depart with Bashful Affection and Gentle Smiles, Visitors Arrive with Old Hatreds and Letters of Sorrow

Now hearing the direction of Mother Liu's words was entirely in favor of the Gan family, the more she spoke, the more angry she became, and she blushed as she said, "Mother Liu, you think people giving you things is a great favor, but in fact, it's just that rich people don't want to throw things into the filthy dirt, and are just using poor people's stomachs to store them. I say, we poor people must fight for this bit of dignity, rather die of hunger than eat other people's leftovers." Jiang Clan glared at her, looking at her and saying, "Our old girl, that's just her temperament, quick-mouthed and quick-tongued, no matter if these words can be said or not, she has to say them. For example, people are kind enough to give you something to eat, whether you want it or not, you have to temporarily accept it on the surface. You can't possibly let Mother Gan give you something and you throw it on the ground." Mother Liu was originally a little embarrassed by Gui Zhi's bold and unreserved words. Now that Jiang Clan rushed to explain it to her, this was considered to have room for maneuver. So she laughed and said, "It's still our old sister-in-law who speaks the truth. You think we poor people can afford not to look at the faces of rich people at all, how can that be possible?" Jiang Clan said, "To speak frankly, their old man might have a little bit of official airs. As for their Mrs. Gan, she's the same as us, just people in the bedroom, relying on people to prosper, following people to suffer, what else is there to say?" Saying it like this gave Mother Liu even more room to maneuver, and she thought that since Ji Zhi often came here, his mother and daughter might have a good relationship with Gan Ji Zhi, so she said, "That Second Master Gan is very good." Jiang Clan knew that her daughter was most deeply stimulated by Ji Zhi, and these words would take her life, so she absolutely dared not bring up those relationship-related words, and just snorted. However, Mother Liu was completely unaware of these reasons, and she became excited and continued to say these words. (191)

Imitating Others

— Yiyi Guan Zhu

I remember when I was a child, I saw this lesson in a textbook: "There was a merchant selling hats, carrying a load of hats of all sizes, and stopped at the foot of a mountain to rest. At the foot of the mountain there was a big tree, but there were many monkeys on that big tree. Seeing the merchant selling hats wearing a hat on his head, they felt it was novel, so they came down from the tree together and robbed the load of hats, putting them all on their heads and escaping up the tree. Later, the merchant selling hats, in desperation, quickly took off the hat he was wearing on his head and threw it on the ground, so the monkeys on the tree, seeing it, also threw down the hats they had robbed and were wearing on their heads!" This is "imitating others."

Originally, monkeys are most fond of imitating others, which is not surprising. What is strange is that those knowledgeable "people" often imitate others in many ways. Now, for example: Westerners and Westerners, when they meet each other, of course, love to speak English, jibber-jabber. However, there are many people who are clearly Chinese and Chinese, and when they meet and talk, instead of speaking the very good "Mandarin," they must speak that jibber-jabbering "foreign language!" This is also "imitating others."

Then there is "dancing," "kissing," "eating Western food," "using foreign goods," and there is no end to these things. In short, whether it is customs, human feelings, clothing, eating and drinking, and all kinds of enjoyment; everything that is stained with Western colors is considered "Europeanization" by the fashionable people, but if you take off the Western lens, what is not "imitating others"? The so-called "Europeanization" is just a nice word.

Although we know that Japan's Meiji Restoration also looked at Europe and the United States as examples, and learned from Europe and the United States as models, and now only a few decades have passed, it has suddenly jumped into the ranks of the world's great powers. Looking at it this way, "imitating others" is not necessarily undesirable. However, it depends on what kind of example you are looking at and what kind of model you are learning. If you look at other people's bad examples and learn other people's superficialities, then what is the difference from the monkeys' "imitating others"?

Little Knowledge

About Bees

— Shen Yan

One spring, I unfortunately suffered from a very dangerous illness. After the illness, the doctor repeatedly told me that I must recuperate in another place to prevent a relapse. So, for fear of death, I hid myself in a small town near Kunshan. The town's residents, including the public security bureau's police station and several small temples, numbered less than fifty families. After 7 p.m. or on rainy days, you could not hear a single human voice. Life was certainly very difficult. Fortunately, next door to the house I lived in, a Mr. Su was raising several boxes of bees, as if it were a recreation arranged especially for me in advance. Every morning, I would rush over to watch, and I would continue to watch after eating, and I would not go back until it was dark and there were no bees to watch. After watching like this for dozens of days, I began to understand the greatness of bees.

In short, bees are really the most diligent and orderly animals. In their group, except for the larvae, no one can survive without working. They all have a queen, and everyone loyally and carefully supports it. Every year, before setting out to collect honey, all the worker bees line up in rows outside the hive, facing the hive, waiting for the queen's inspection. After the inspection, those who should collect honey go to collect honey, those who should return to the hive to protect the larvae return to the hive, and those who should take on the guard duty outside the hive stay outside without leaving for a moment, and none of them will wander around. What is even more strange is that every bee must greet the guard bee when entering and exiting the hole, and it seems that there is a fixed time. Once the fixed time has passed, no one is allowed to enter or exit. Once, in order to show me the strict discipline of the bees, Mr. Su specially caught a bee, put him in a small box, and after a night, put a dot on him with a vermilion pen, and then released him back. An hour later, when we went to the front of each hive to look, we found that the bee with the vermilion dot was lying dead on the ground in front of a certain hive, of course, because he did not return overnight, so he was stung to death by the guard bee. Our experiment was successful, but unfortunately, this bee was killed by us.

Whenever a new queen is born, the old queen (i.e., the mother of the new queen) must take all the new worker bees away from the hive the next day, and let the old worker bees serve the new queen. The night before, the hive must be restless all night, buzzing as if they were saying goodbye. Therefore, when beekeepers encounter this situation, they must prepare a new hive the next morning to allow the old queen to settle down, otherwise this group of bees will never return. Two different groups of bees will inevitably start a fierce battle when they meet. But after the end of the war, the victorious bees will automatically take on the burial work. They use their feet to hook some dead bees from the ground, all the way to the cracks in the tiles paved on the surface, and carefully hide them; one by one, they will not let go until all the bee corpses are hidden.

Most insects respect the female, and bees are of course the same. The queen bee and the worker bees are all female, but the worker bees have a stinger on their tail, so they cannot mate. After the queen bee is born, she only mates once, and once she has mated, she can never mate again, but she can give birth endlessly. The mating situation is also very special. First, a virgin queen bee flies back and forth alone in the air, and soon many drones swarm over to pursue her. The word "pursue" is really the most appropriate. Because as soon as the queen bee sees the drones coming, she immediately runs away, and the drones naturally chase after her desperately. Whoever catches her first, the victory belongs to whoever. But extreme joy leads to sorrow. When the mating is over, his reproductive organs get stuck in the queen bee's tail and can no longer be pulled out. As a result, the queen bee takes his reproductive organs away, and this bee becomes a romantic ghost who dies under a peony flower. However, after this mating, the queen bee can never mate again.

Education News

Painful Commemoration of September 18th

The Citywide Middle School Student Union: The Shanghai Municipal Middle School Student Union held a meeting yesterday morning at 9:00 at the auditorium of the Xiaoximen Youth Propaganda Team to commemorate September 18th. Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, Yu Zhongbiao, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, and more than 200 student members from Jingye, Fudan, Qingxin, Minli, Junyi, Shanghai Girls' Middle School, Minli Girls' Middle School, Datong High School Attached, Guangxia, and other schools attended. Wang Degeng of Fudan Middle School presided over the meeting, and Zeng Zhaohua took the minutes. The ceremony was carried out as usual. First, the chairman reported the significance of holding the September 18th commemoration. Then, Yu Zhongbiao, the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, gave a speech on the process of the September 18th incident, the significance of commemorating September 18th, and the future efforts of young students. At the same time, he hoped to unite with sincerity to save the country and the nation. Next, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, Pan Gongzhan, gave a speech, roughly divided into two points: (1) To save the country, we must first have organization; (2) Young people should have a spirit of hard work. His words were very painful. Finally, representatives from Guangxia Middle School, Qi Shoushan, Fudan Middle School, Fan Chongbi, and Junyi Middle School, Zhou Chengmei, spoke successively. The meeting lasted until about 12:00 noon.

Citizen Education Center: The Shanghai Citizen Education Center, in order to commemorate the painful September 18th Incident and encourage the public's anti-Japanese ideas, held a September 18th Commemoration Meeting in the lecture hall at 2:00 p.m. yesterday. More than 600 people attended. Despite the old wind and rain, the participants were still very enthusiastic. After the ceremony was carried out as usual, Director Chen of the center first reported the significance of the meeting. Then, Chen Bai, the representative of the Municipal Education Bureau, gave a speech. Next, former Korean Consul Zhang Weicheng was invited to speak on the remote and recent causes of the September 18th Incident and the course of the incident, which was vividly described and moved the audience. Subsequently, a pantomime ("Struggle"), martial arts ("Sharpening Must"), and a costume performance ("Love and Blood") were performed, which were vivid and moving.

University Federation: The Shanghai University Student Union's ninth radio broadcast to save the country was held at 5:00 p.m. yesterday at the Zhongxi Pharmacy Radio Station. Xiao Guanglie of Jinan University gave a lecture entitled "How to Save the Country."

Jiaotong University: Jiaotong University students yesterday divided into two groups to commemorate September 18th, both with grief and solemnity. Both groups were presided over by Chen Shouquan, the school's dean of discipline, with speeches by the school's president, Li Yaosheng, and the academic dean, Zhang Gongjiu.

Sino-French Engineering College: The Sino-French National Engineering College held an opening ceremony at 8:30 a.m. yesterday. All the faculty, staff, and more than 300 students gathered together. After the ceremony was carried out as usual, President Chu Minyi reported the examination results for the 20th to 22nd academic years. A total of nine students were promoted to the fourth grade of university, fourteen students were promoted to the third grade, seventeen students were promoted to the second grade, and twenty-two students were promoted to the first grade. About 100 students from the senior high school and French language tutoring classes were promoted. Eighty-six new students were recruited for the tutoring class. After the summer vacation next year, the school will have a class of university students graduating. Then, a lecture was given on the significance of commemorating September 18th.

Jianguo Middle School: Jianguo Middle School on Zhiyuan Road in Zhabei held a memorial meeting at Jizhe Hall yesterday to mark the second anniversary of the "September 18th" incident. The principal's office announced the memorial measures in advance, ordering students not to ask for leave to go out. All the speeches of the memorial meeting chairman and professors must be recorded and submitted that night to score the students, which will be used as part of the Chinese language accumulation. At the memorial meeting, presided over by Principal Chen, he reported on the significance of commemorating September 18th in detail. Professors Wang Jinchan and students Jia Ding, etc., then gave speeches.

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 18th) Zhu Kezhen, Director of the Institute of Meteorology of the Academia Sinica, after representing China at the Pacific Science Conference in Canada, participated in the Chicago Centennial Celebration and visited various countries in Europe, including England, France, Germany, Italy, Norway, and Sweden, to observe the latest meteorological equipment. Jiangsu Province's Education Budget for the 22nd Year: Regular and Temporary Expenses Increased Compared to the Previous Year

The Jiangsu Province's education expenditure budget for the 21st year, including the three special funds of field tax, slaughter tax, and broker tax, totaled 3.8 million yuan. Combined with 200,000 yuan from administrative income and 300,000 yuan in subsidies from the provincial treasury, the total was 4.3 million yuan. In the 22nd year, the field tax will be increased by 80,000 yuan to 2.52 million yuan, the slaughter tax will be increased by 50,000 yuan to 650,000 yuan, and the broker tax will be increased by 20,000 yuan to 630,000 yuan, totaling 3.95 million yuan (an increase of 150,000 yuan from field tax, slaughter tax, and broker tax). Combined with 200,000 yuan from administrative income and 300,000 yuan in subsidies from the provincial treasury, the total budget for this year is set at:

Revenue side: 4.45 million yuan.

Expenditure side: (Regular expenses) amounted to 3,558,340 yuan, categorized as follows: (1) Higher education expenses: 279,902 yuan (including expenses for specialized normal schools, fisheries schools, the National Studies Library, subsidies for the Science Society of China, and study abroad expenses); (2) General education expenses: 2,543,536 yuan (divided into four items: 1. Secondary schools: 2,096,407 yuan; 2. Primary schools and compulsory education expenses: 383,520 yuan; 3. Subsidies for Nanching Middle School and other middle schools, normal schools, vocational schools for boys and girls, and kindergartens: 35,992 yuan; 4. Special projects for primary and secondary schools, such as study tours, participation in sports meets, scouting inspections, and travel expenses for other meetings convened by the department, tuition fees for children of revolutionary martyrs, and other special projects: 27,617 yuan); (3) Social education expenses: 624,212 yuan (divided into: 1. Social education institutions: 577,400 yuan; 2. Social education projects: 22,200 yuan; 3. Subsidy expenses: 24,612 yuan); (4) Other institutions and administrative projects: 110,784 yuan. (Temporary expenses) amounted to 891,566 yuan (including 453,000 yuan for offsetting accumulated deficits and reserve funds for actual temporary items), categorized as follows: ) General education temporary expenses: 393,000 yuan; (2) Social education temporary expenses: 60,000 yuan; (3) Offsetting accumulated deficits from previous years: 140,000 yuan; (4) Reserve funds: 298,566 yuan (the reserve fund listed in the previous year was 298,248 yuan).

Comparison of two years: Last year's field tax, slaughter tax, broker tax, administrative income, and provincial subsidies totaled 4.3 million yuan. This year, the three items of field tax, slaughter tax, and broker tax increased by 150,000 yuan, with total revenue of 4.45 million yuan. On the expenditure side, except for the repayment of old debts, which was listed at over 400,000 yuan last year and 140,000 yuan this year, which is less, the regular expenses for each item have increased due to the expansion of projects in the 22nd year. For example, the implementation of the integration of training and education in primary and secondary schools requires an increase of 100,000 yuan to revise the budget standards, 60,000 yuan for the additional grades of primary and secondary schools, 20,000 yuan for establishing rural normal schools, increasing promotion fees for provincial primary schools, preparing experimental areas for compulsory education, adding experimental areas for mass education, transforming the pottery engineering department of Yixing Vocational School into a junior ceramic vocational school, the Jingjiang Mass Education Center, recovering the Yu Tang Mass Education Center, and various social education special projects and administrative projects. The total increase in regular expenses compared to the previous year is estimated to be over 380,000 yuan. The temporary expense budget, in addition to the originally listed repair and equipment fees for primary and secondary schools, the expansion equipment fees for vocational schools and vocational departments of middle schools, and the temporary expenses for social education, which still need to be listed in the 22nd year (the originally listed establishment fees for specialized normal schools and the establishment fees for Suzhou Industrial School will no longer be listed, except for a portion that will still be listed for Suzhou Industrial School), the added expenses include the equipment fees for the weaving machines in the dyeing and weaving factory of Suzhou Industrial School, the purchase of fishing vessels for the fisheries school, and the repayment of the loan for the silk reeling equipment of the Women's Sericulture School. The increase in temporary expenses compared to the previous year is estimated to be about 88,000 yuan.

Provincial Department Relief: After the Education Department of Jiangsu Province decided on the above budget at the Jiangsu Education Expenditure Committee meeting, it immediately notified the Education Expenditure Management Office. Considering the accumulated deficits over the years and the practice of spending future income, it feared that income would not cover expenses. Therefore, it proposed 350,000 yuan from the temporary expense portion and 50,000 yuan from the regular expense portion to be designated for offsetting accumulated deficits, noting that the allocation should be temporarily suspended to leave room for flexibility. This matter will be submitted by the Education Department to the next Education Expenditure Committee meeting for discussion and decision, and to seek a comprehensive plan for other revenue sources and relief. Before the submission for discussion, the Education Department has the authority to allocate the province's education budget, so there is not much of a problem.

School Difficulties: This year's temporary expenses are only 453,000 yuan, of which 350,000 yuan has been temporarily proposed, leaving 103,000 yuan. Each school and social education institution has projects that urgently need to be carried out and equipment that needs to be repaired. It is heard that the principals of provincial schools held a meeting on the 15th and discussed ways to increase funding and will make suggestions. If a complete solution is to be found, a temporary meeting of the Education Expenditure Committee must be convened, as the committee is required to meet every few months according to regulations, which would be too slow to address the urgent need.

All sports experts in Nanjing will be hired nearby to save expenses. (2) The committee has learned from previous sports meets that disputes have arisen from the refereeing aspect. The referees hired this time will be selected based on their experience, knowledge, and reputation in the sports world.

Shanghai City Games Ball Games

Women's Volleyball Finals: Wuben Defeats Haixing

But the championship is still a pending case, awaiting review and resolution by the organizing committee. Men's Volleyball: Although Xiaguang Defeated Dongya, It is Still Considered a Forfeit.

31 Participants in Men's Singles Tennis, Starting Tomorrow. Numbers for Track and Field and National Arts to be Issued Starting This Afternoon.

The ball game competition of the 3rd Shanghai City Games was held yesterday, the third day. Affected by the strong winds and rain, the outdoor competitions, such as soccer, tennis, and softball, were all suspended. The volleyball competition was moved to the indoor venue of the China Basketball Hall. In both competitions, the issue of player eligibility arose. The Xiaguang team used unregistered players such as Xu Heng and Gu Shangxiang to compete. As a result, although they defeated Dongya, it was still considered a forfeit, and Dongya regained the qualification for the semi-finals. In the women's volleyball final between Haixing and Wuben, it was claimed that Guo Xiaoping of the Haixing team was a physical education teacher from a certain school, which violated the amateur regulations. The Minli team filed a protest. This matter has not yet been resolved and needs to be reviewed by the review committee at a meeting. Before the issue is resolved, the matter will be explained to both Haixing and Wuben teams, and the competition will proceed as usual. If it is confirmed that Guo Xiaoping's qualifications do violate the amateur rules, then the match between Haixing and Minli should be considered a forfeit by Haixing, and Minli and Wuben will compete in the final. The result of yesterday's match was that Wuben won 3-1 and won the city championship. If Guo's qualification is not a problem, the championship will still belong to Wuben; otherwise, the championship cannot be resolved and must be determined by the final between Minli and Wuben.

This afternoon, the semi-finals of the men's volleyball will be held, and there will be matches in soccer and women's tennis singles and doubles. However, if the weather does not cooperate, it may be difficult to hold them on time. The women's softball final will be held in the China Basketball Hall. Xu Heng of Jinan is a Famous General

His Skills on the Net are a Sight to Behold

In the men's group, Xiaguang played against Dongya first. In the first set, Xiaguang used all Daxia players, who were heavily pressured by Dongya and lost 8-21. Xiaguang reversed the defeat and won. However, because Xu Heng and others were not registered, Xiaguang was immediately ruled to forfeit, and Dongya benefited from misfortune and won the victory. Jiangsu Provincial Games to Open Today

More Than 680 Male and Female Athletes from 13 Districts Across the Province Participating

Men's and Women's Track and Field Competitions and Ball Games All Begin Today

Districts 2 and 3 Have the Strongest Strength and Are Most Likely to Win the Men's and Women's Championship

(Zhenjiang, 18th Dispatch) The Jiangsu Provincial Games are scheduled to open in the province today (the 19th). Participating units include all 13 administrative districts of the province, with a total of 685 male and female athletes. All participants have reported and are residing in the Land Surveying Personnel Training Institute and the Provincial People's Education Hall Clubhouse. The games will last for four days, concluding on the 22nd. This is the third provincial games of Jiangsu Province, serving as a preliminary selection for this year's National Games. Athletes from all districts are the elite of their respective regions, and a competition is sure to bring about excellent performances.

Competing Units

The competition is organized by administrative inspectorate districts, with the counties under each unit as follows: District 1, Zhenjiang, Danyang, Jurong, Jintan, Yangzhong, Lishui, Gaochun, Jiangning; District 2, Wujin, Wuxi, Yixing, Jiangyin, Liyang; District 3, Wuxian, Changshu, Kunshan, Wujiang; District 4, Songjiang, Qingpu, Jinshan, Fengxian; District 5, Shanghai, Nanhui, Chuansha; District 6, Jiading, Taicang, Baoshan; District 7, Nantong, Rugao, Haimen, Chongming, Qidong; District 8, Taixian, Dongtai, Taixing, Jingjiang; District 9, Jiangdu, Gaoyou, Baoying, Yizheng, Liuhe, Jiangpu; District 10, Yancheng, Funing, Xinghua; District 11, Huaiyin, Huaian, Lianshui, Siyang, Suqian; District 12, Tongshan, Fengxian, Peixian, Xiaoxian, Dangshan, Pixian, Suining; District 13, Donghai, Guanyun, Shuyang, Ganyu.

Championship Categories

The tournament championships are divided into male and female sections. The men's group includes seven categories: field events, track events, all-around, soccer, basketball, tennis, and volleyball. The women's group includes five categories: track and field, basketball, tennis, volleyball, and softball. The gender divisions with the most championship wins will each be awarded the overall championship. Chinese martial arts is a separate championship.

District Strengths

Comparing the past competition results of each district, the second and third districts have the strongest strength, followed by the first and sixth districts. Districts two and three are full of talented individuals, and many of them are outstanding. It is generally recognized that the overall championship will be contended for by these districts. The second district has a stronger hold on track and field all-around events, while the third district is slightly better in ball games. The first district has very few talented people, so its hopes are slim, but it may be able to get third place. The other districts have average results, making it difficult to distinguish between them. As for the individuals, there are notables such as Lu Yaxiong from the sixth district, Wang Wenjin from the second district in the sprint, long jump, Jin Zhongkang from the second district in long-distance running, Zhang Jia from the second district in the triple jump, Gui Zhongfei from the third district in the pole vault, and Zhu Mengchang from the third district in the triathlon. Not only can they break provincial records, but they can also compete with famous players in the National Games.
