Free Talk

(Roar, China!) Behind the Scenes

— Xu Maoyong

The original author, S. Tretyakov, said: (These are all facts; I have not changed anything. Moreover, the case itself is a characteristic!)

Yes, these are facts, these are the facts that we are accustomed to seeing: this is a characteristic, but this is a characteristic that we have overlooked.

This familiarity with the facts and neglect of the characteristics can explain why the author of such a drama is Russian and not Chinese. Precisely because we are accustomed to the tyranny (of the white imperialists), it has become commonplace, and our writers have neglected it and do not see any characteristics. But to outsiders, especially Russians, it is naturally clear.

We do have (revolutionary literature) and (national literature). But what this literature always tells us is that certain (revolutionaries) and (national heroes) are leading and commanding, so the revolution has risen, and the national movement has risen. And then? We only see the joys and sorrows of the revolutionaries and national heroes, mostly interspersed with romance. As for the revolution and the national movement, it is always (in a place where the clouds are deep and one cannot tell).

This drama tells us the truth about (who is roaring?) (how did they start roaring?).

But I think the most useful lesson for us is the author's words: (Cities repeatedly saved from foreign cannons were finally destroyed by them in 1926.) If we want to preserve everything, we will ultimately fail, so we might as well break like jade. Therefore, the author loudly appeals (Roar, China!)

Regarding the public performance by the Drama Cooperative, I also want to say a few words. Namely, such a public performance is still far from the goal of (being demanded by the public). In China, such a ticket price can only be performed in the cities, and therefore can only be used as a momentary stimulant for the petty bourgeoisie.

However, I do not intend to disrespect the current drama movement. I greatly admire the goal and the efforts. I only hope that those engaged in this movement will work harder to approach that goal.

Fan Chengda and Liu Dabai

— He Ru

Flipping through the Stone Lake Poetry Collection by chance, I feel that the (Grand Chancellor) Fan Chengda, who was (highly respected by all officials and famous throughout the world), is like Liu Dabai. Although he was an official, he was quite sympathetic to farmers, peddlers, beggars, and artisans. However, Liu Dabai was born in modern times, and his poems slightly add a bit of social thought, as if he is learning the latest fashion. Moreover, after becoming an official, he was unwilling to write poems like "Peddling Cloth Ballad," what he was willing to write about was how to improve official documents written in Mandarin. His beautiful old dream was shattered by the vulgar official language.

Speaking of Liu Dabai's old dreams, these are the same as those of many modern talented men and beautiful women, nothing more than things like love and revolution, commonplaces of new life that people repeat from others. It is not necessary to say that this is an old saying. He became the Vice Minister of Education, and the revolution can be considered a success, but he never compared the ancient version to what he longed for in the world. Although love has poetry as proof, I have not seen the sequel. Naturally, living in today's world, taking a concubine while being an official is something that should be in the "Official's Guide." Why bother with love in such a twisted manner?

Fan Chengda was also a refined official. When we read his Stone Lake lyrics, we can roughly see his enjoyment of life as a (young libertine) who (fears feeling old as flowers age). Because we already know that something called (lyrics) is precisely the living literature that was popular in that era, like the tunes of today's (light drizzle), which should be listed in the art of the leisure class. Without the fortune to enjoy the life of fine wine, beautiful women, and singing, one is out of touch with this type of art. Liu Dabai, who was born in modern times, refused to follow the poets of the light drizzle school, but wanted to fill in a few vernacular lyrics and become a pioneer of (the liberation of lyrics), which can be said to have misled others. Who has seen the sound of a piano in a modern dance hall singing lyrics of liberation?

It is said that Liu Dabai was impoverished after his death and almost had no way to arrange a funeral. If this is true, then it is something we should deeply lament. There seem to be few (disaster officials) who have become high officials and still have no money to buy a coffin after death. Although the Ministry of Education is a relatively clean government office, the minister and vice minister should not be so poor. Fan Chengda naturally became extremely wealthy when he became an official like a prime minister. He had a villa called Stone Lake, which was inscribed by the emperor, and he called himself the Stone Lake Recluse. His friend Yang Wanli said: (The scenery of Stone Lake is the most beautiful in the southeast.) So he was a big landlord. But I don't know if Liu Dabai, living in Hangzhou, had a villa on West Lake?

Liu Dabai's opposition to ghost-writing and writing vernacular poetry is not surprising after the May Fourth Movement. Fan Chengda happened to be born in an era when Taoist scholars and corrupt Confucianists were gradually rising, vernacular quotations came out, and Taoist poems close to the vernacular came out. Even the Jianghu poetry school, which used current events as allusions, also appeared. His poetry wanted to use simple and natural words, which is also nothing unusual. However, he liked to sing about pastoral landscapes and did not raise the bones of holy scriptures and virtuous traditions to scare living people, which is where he was a little more brilliant than those Confucian poets of his time.

I believe that Fan Chengda's pastoral poems can very well represent the feudal landlord class's appreciation, praise, longing for, and sorrow for the beauty of the countryside and nature. To use an analogy, it is like a wealthy person who is tired of eating chicken, duck, and fish and envies the vegetables and tofu eaten by the poor. However, from a small part of his poems, it can still be seen that he cares about the farmers who are trapped in difficulties and groaning at the bottom of the darkness. Opening granaries to provide disaster relief and ordering the elimination of locusts, although there are poems as proof, are ultimately official articles written as an official. "Urging the Rent Collection" writes about the corvée imposed by the village chiefs (grass sandal fee), and "Following Urging the Rent Collection" writes about the disaster victims being unable to pay taxes and even selling their clothes and daughters. These are all considered poems calling for the poor farmers. Also, the miserable cries of peddlers often made him sad, and he could not help but compose a poem. He said: (The medicine seller outside the wall has not missed a single day in nine years. His singing voice is very suitable. I asked him in the snow, and he has ten mouths in his family. If he does not go out for a day, he will be hungry and cold.) His poem is:

Ten mouths cry and blame deeply, how can they sit peacefully with felt needles. Loudly singing and yelling to deceive the wind and snow, it is not willing but bitter.

This seems to be much more brilliant than artists like Mr. Feng Zikai, who appreciate old and sick beggars like Millet's famous paintings (see "Random Notes from the Edge Hall"). Let me record two short poems by Stone Lake:

Driven out by hungry bellies, daring not to be idle? Snow legs and icy whiskers, accustomed to enduring the cold. It's not that they can't sit behind closed doors, enduring the cold is still bearable, but enduring hunger is difficult.

Crying and begging for a small amount is worth a thousand gold, frozen sparrows and hungry crows share the same sound. Laboring you to this point in life, what is the heart of the vast universe!

This was written when he heard the cries of those selling fish and vegetables outside the wall in the snow, who were struggling greatly to make a sale, and he was moved to write it. If he really attributed this social phenomenon of labor and poverty to the fortune of heaven, it would make modern revolutionaries laugh. Let me record another poem by him, "Singers on the River Market":

How can they be leisurely singing the "Weicheng Song"? There must be injustice in it. Pitying their hungry faces at dusk, they strongly pretend to be in the depths of spring, seeking friends' voices.

Fan Shihu also knew that the poor class had their cries of injustice. Therefore, I always feel that the speculative revolutionary poems of modern people like Liu Dabai, from "Peddling Cloth Ballad" onwards, have nothing remarkable. At most, it can only be said that their thoughts are a little more progressive than those of Bai Juyi and Fan Shihu, and they still have to thank the lessons of the times.

Two Occasional Thoughts

— Tang

(1) Biographical Literature

I felt something after reading Mr. Yu Dafu's biographical literature a few days ago. I am writing it to ask for advice from several experts who write autobiographies and critical biographies.

Mr. Yu seems to regret that there is no better biography in the current literary world. In fact, this is only natural. What a biography needs is a thorough account of all the events and a calm, detached mind, so it is especially suitable to be written after death.

New literature has been popular for only a little over ten years at most. Most of the pioneering scholars are still alive, and some are in the process of transformation, starting anew (?). They used to ridicule and point fingers, but now they sing praises and support them. They used to abandon the main road, but now they have embarked on the broad road, from heretics to orthodoxy. Whether there will be further changes in the future, even Liu Bowen would find it difficult to predict. If one were to write a biography or account for them at this time, obliterating the causes and consequences, it would make people uneasy!

As for the popular ones on the market recently, they are mostly about where the person is from, how many brothers they have, how many bowls of rice they eat per meal, whether the nose is between the eyes, and so on. Other than that, there is no vitality at all, as if entering the mountain gate and looking up, everyone has the face of a Bodhisattva.

Originally, getting a few friends to praise each other, or praising famous people higher to advance oneself, is the origin of critical biographies. If no one writes a critical biography, or if what is said in the critical biography is not conducive to oneself, then one takes up the pen and blows oneself up in a majestic manner, which is said to be an autobiography.

Friends are afraid of hurting friendships, unknown writers want to take this opportunity to advance themselves, and people want to take the opportunity to promote themselves, all because of being alive.

Therefore, if we say that the yellow race is not inferior to the white race, then to have good biographies, one only needs to hope that those fickle famous people die sooner.

(2) Morality is Lost

It is said that starting from October 1st, the official documents of the provincial and municipal governments will use new punctuation marks. At the same time, lawyers' pleadings and court judgments will also be rewritten in the vernacular. As a result, those who care about the world will inevitably have more articles of lament on their pens.

This is really helpless. (Heaven is about to destroy culture), this is really helpless!

From the May Fourth Movement to the present, domestic traditional writing has been stumbling along, closely following the new literature, already exhausted. But this year is, after all, a memorable year. (Six or seven sage rulers appeared), some people advocate reading the classics, and others advocate restoration. In their spare time from politics, they form societies to compose poems. In this prosperous era of cultural governance, the descendants of Confucianism are all rejoicing, believing that the sage's doctrines will be seen again today.

Unexpectedly, not long after, the (what-is-it-then) new literature was actually selected. This somersault has caused cries of suffering.

Therefore: (Alas, culture is lost!)

Talk of a Bibliophile

— A Ying

(10)

Ten years ago, I bought a copy of (Shi's Commentary on Du Fu's Poetry) with the handwriting of the Zha family of Jingxian County, a book collection, read by Zimu, and chapters by Zha Rihua, etc. When I returned home and flipped through it, I was overjoyed to find that it actually contained a business card of Mei Zengliang and a short note in Mei Zengliang's own handwriting. The short note read:

I am now packing my books, and there are quite a few that are too heavy. The Su Poetry that I bought for eight copper coins, if you need it, brother, I can let you have it, and I don't even need the original price. If you have already bought it, please let me know. I wish you a good day. Yours sincerely, Mei Zengliang.

At that time, I lent this note to the Commercial Press to be published in (Novel World) Volume 13. The business card was of course the old Chinese style, printed with the three characters (Mei Zengliang) in woodcut, on vermilion paper, with a few words added, which were for sending lotus root powder to Zha Zimu. From this, I knew that the (Su Poetry) I bought was actually from Mei Zengliang's collection. Famous people selling books, in this short note, can be said to have gained another interest.

Shallow Lake (9)

— Written by Joseph Conrad of England, Translated by Shi Hang

In this deep silence, Asad's voice vibrated high.

(I got her! I got her! To get her, I dare to face all mankind. But I got her! Then --

His words echoed towards the empty distance. He stopped, as if quietly listening to the sound disappearing into the distant distance -- there was no way to call it back. Then he said quietly --

(Tuan, I love my brother.)

A gust of wind made me shiver. Above his head, on the quiet sea of clouds, the palm leaves rubbed together, making a mournful and desperate sound. The white man spread his legs. His chin rested on his chest, and then he did not raise his head and muttered sadly --

(We all love our brothers.)

Asad shouted in a low but excited tone --

(What do I care about the death of others? What I want is peace in my own heart.)

He seemed to hear a sound in the house, listened quietly, and quietly walked in. The white man stood up. A gust of wind blew past with excitement. The stars flickered more dimly, as if they had retreated into the solidified depths of vast space. After a cold wind blew past, half the sky was completely silent and absolutely quiet. After that, behind the dark and winding lines of the forest, a pillar of golden light radiated from the heavens and spread into a semicircle on the eastern horizon. The sun rose. The clouds also cleared, forming floating fragments, and disappearing into thin flying breaths. At this time, the shallow lake was uncovered, and under the roots of the trees, in the thick shadows, it was dark and glowing. A white eagle, tilting upwards, flew into the clear intestinal light, showing a dazzling brilliance for a moment, and then flew higher, before it disappeared into the azure blue, becoming a thick black and static spot, as if it had left the world forever. The white man, standing in front of the door, stared at the world, and heard intermittent and chaotic murmurs in the hut, and finally a painful groan. Suddenly, Asad, with his hands outstretched, staggered out, trembling all over, his eyes fixed and standing still for a while. Then he said --

(She no longer has a fever.)

Grains: Rumors of Increased Taxes on Foreign Rice and Wheat; Futures Flour and Wheat Accelerate Rapidly

In the flour market, both the morning and afternoon openings showed a consistent and sharp rise, with foreign wheat prices rebounding by 1.1 yuan in Chicago and around 0.4 yuan in Canada. Therefore, the market mood had already stabilized at the opening. Then, rumors spread that the government would implement increased taxes on foreign rice and wheat, so outsiders were also encouraged, leading to exploitation. Prices for each month were better by over 1 fen. By the afternoon, the buying interest in each month was even more active. It was said that miscellaneous grain merchants from both local and foreign ports were buying particularly aggressively, causing near and far-term prices to soar step by step. On the mill side, it was heard that Fuxin had released a small amount, while others remained inactive. Tianjin quoted a small 0.2 fen, opening at 2.28 yuan. As a result, the current month was up 2.5 fen compared to the previous week, October was up 3.25 fen, November/December were up 3.375 fen, January was up 3.25 fen, and February was up 4 fen.

In the wheat market, the morning and afternoon openings showed an initial stabilization followed by a sharp rise, with foreign wheat prices rebounding by 0.4 yuan to 1.1 yuan. Therefore, the market sentiment had already stabilized at the opening. Then, rumors spread that foreign rice and wheat would be subject to increased taxes, with a proposed increase of 1.5 yuan per dan of rice. Grain traders from both local and foreign ports paid attention to this situation, and buying in each month also turned smooth, causing market prices to soar step by step. Although flour sales remained sluggish, speculators did not consider whether this kind of relief would be needed in the future. The implementation of the dumping tax has already been reported, but it has not yet been agreed upon. Now, the authorities are actively proceeding with it because the domestic flour price is falling and the rural areas are in danger. Yesterday, according to news from the Guangzhou Chaozhou Shantou merchants, Guangdong Province first implemented the opening of a small tax, collecting a dumping tax of one yuan per 100 catties of foreign rice. Calculating at 150 catties per stone, it would be necessary to add 1.5 yuan. Future sources would inevitably be cut off, and with the foreign rice route cut off, they would only seek the output of the five provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Hunan in the country's producing areas. The Chaozhou merchants were smoothly processing the Wuhu, and yesterday, the Wuhu prices soared by more than half a yuan. It is said that the Guangdong, Fujian, and Guangxi provinces are contacting Hunan Province to directly handle the loading, so the producing areas are all reporting price increases. The rice in Shanghai is especially noted by the Southern merchants. The new Heshang rice has already been inquired about by Guangdong and Fujian. Customers Xian bought 1,000 bales of Nanjing railway Xian by the Shantou merchants yesterday, with the price at 7.1 to 7.02 yuan. The Shantou merchants were still in the initial trial stage. The Fujian merchants were processing 1,000 bales of Kunshan sheep at a price of 7.3 to 7.18 yuan. 115 bales of Hunan machine Jing were purchased at a price of 7 yuan, and 109 bales of brown rice were purchased at a price of 5 yuan jiao ban. Chen Xiaojiao, who had long been abandoned by the customers, was rushed to be processed by the Ningbo merchants yesterday at a price that had returned to 6.75 yuan, which was 7 fen higher than last week. It is said that the Xiang Jing machine Xian suddenly rose by more than half a yuan.

New Yellow Beans are Scarce and the Market is Stable

New yellow beans were previously sluggish due to the surge of goods, but recently, not many have arrived, and the inventory has been thin. Sales have also been sluggish. Yesterday, the total market turnover was over 300 bales of Jiujiang beans, 600 bales of Hankou beans, one vehicle of Changzhou beans, and 400 bales of Jiangbei beans. Therefore, the market cannot improve, only slightly better by 2-3 fen compared to before.

Oil Market: Camphor Oil Market Depressed

Camphor oil is usually in high demand during the autumn harvesting season, so the market is typically active after autumn. Traders anticipate that autumn sales will boost the market and prices will rise. However, contrary to expectations, sales have remained sluggish even after autumn. Although the supply from Wuhan is limited, the total inventory exceeds 30,000 dan (a unit of weight). Compared to past Wuhan market trends, this is not a large amount, but the slow sales are unprecedented. Those with inventory are understandably anxious. According to yesterday's information from Wuhan, premium camphor oil has dropped by about 22 yuan, while standard camphor oil is slightly above 21 yuan, and Macheng camphor oil is at 20.07-0.08 yuan, a decrease of about one yuan compared to last week. Shanghai merchants, anticipating autumn sales, have maintained substantial inventories. However, due to sluggish sales and widespread reports of weakness in various regions, selling prices have been continuously reduced. Although the trade association has set a fixed price, it is treated as a mere formality, and the market prices are in complete disarray.

Silk and Tea: Yellow and White Filature Supplementing French Orders

(Abundant Autumn Cocoon Shipments to Shanghai from Zhejiang) The autumn cocoon markets in Hangzhou, Shaoxing, Huzhou, and Jiaxing in Zhejiang province are gradually closing. The fresh cocoons collected by various cocoon merchants are being dried and actively transported to Shanghai by both land and water routes. Recently, the section of the Suzhou Creek near the Laopo Bridge has been filled with barges loaded with autumn cocoons, and the warehouses at the South Railway Station are also packed with cocoon bales. The transportation situation is no less bustling than during the spring cocoon season. (Eri Silk Thread Costs are Not Low) Xunzhen (Nanxun and Zhenze) and other places are major producers of Eri silk thread. This year, the price of local silk is high, and silk production is not strong. In the past few months, only 758 bales of dried Eri silk thread have been shipped to Shanghai. The cost of new silk this season is over 700 yuan per bale.

(Artificial Silk Sales Can Be Considered Good) Due to foreign exchange constraints, the price of artificial silk continues to decline. However, sales are still reasonably strong. Yesterday, Jin Qilin (Golden Kirin), Black Beauty, First Grade Red Fish, and other brands were imported from Tianjin with 40 cases of forward goods at a price range of 179.75 to 178.25 yuan net.

(Yellow and White Filature Sales to France Slightly Active) Yesterday, the Shanghai foreign merchants' silk market saw slight activity in sales to France due to continued strong price increases in overseas silk markets, with French firms replenishing their stocks of yellow and white filature silk. New York silk telegraphs were not transmitted, and American firms were waiting for the right time to act. Yesterday, Sincere & Co. and others imported 40 bales of white filature silk and 20 bales of Shandong filature silk at firm prices.

Foreign Merchants' Tea Market Turning Quiet

Yesterday, the Shanghai foreign merchants' tea market turned quiet. British and French merchants have not received responses to the large number of telegrams they sent last week. In addition, yesterday's severe storms and dark skies made it difficult to evaluate various teas. As a result, the standard market became increasingly deserted. Only Tongfu, Yongxing, and other firms, as well as the Russian tea cooperative, purchased a total of over 800 chests of Zhen Mei (Precious Eyebrow) and Gong Xi (Tribute Happiness) teas, with little change in prices.

Piece Goods: Sudden Rise in the Price of Melton Cloth

Melton cloth is most popular in the autumn sales season. Tailors in this district must rush to meet demand until early winter. In addition to the Sichuan merchants, other merchants are currently selecting goods. Melton cloth comes in two colors, Yuan (black) and Chang (navy blue). The inland and local markets mostly sell navy blue, while Sichuan merchants specialize in Yuan (black). The import cost of new goods is quite high, and current selling prices are mostly for old stock. Anyone selling new stock would inevitably incur losses. Due to the abundance of existing inventory, it has been difficult to raise prices. Most merchants who have placed orders have untold grievances. However, the market showed a turnaround yesterday, especially for those holding large stocks of Yuan (black) Melton cloth, who raised prices externally. The sudden rise is attributed to purchases by merchants from Beiping (Beijing). It is said that merchants from Beiping need a large number of Yuan (black) Melton cloth for uniforms, requiring approximately 3,000 to 4,000 yards, and several firms are sourcing it. This has led those holding inventory to become active and collectively raise prices.

Miscellaneous: Recent Import and Export Report

Silk and Tea Exports

(Yangtze River) Imports: In the past two days, approximately 800 pieces of tobacco leaves from Hankou, over 400 pieces of machine-spun cotton, and a total of over 500 barrels of tung oil and tea oil have arrived. Huangdou (soybeans) (400+ bags) and green beans (100+ bags) and eggs (300+ baskets) came from Jiujiang and Wuhu. In addition, there are over 1,000 pieces of tea leaves, which will be shipped to Yingkou and then to Vladivostok.

(Overseas) Approximately 3,000+ pieces of machine oil, iron bars, hardware, and paper arrived from Europe. Exports yesterday included 390 bales of Huzhou silk, 79 pieces of silk waste, 28 pieces of silk fabrics, 16 pieces of sheep intestines, 82 pieces of egg yolks, over 10 pieces of human hair, 85 pieces of cotton yarn waste, 2,375 pieces of tea leaves, and 170 bags of stone powder. 80 pieces of cotton cloth were shipped to South America. Cloth was shipped to Haiti.

Talking Points

Sick

Dry Preface

The weather these past few days has been especially hot, and then the cold suddenly comes very quickly. Now the wind is blowing, now there are a few raindrops. Yu, who has always been physically weak and rushes about the streets all day, could not help but catch a cold and get sick. Sick, really sick!

In order to live, in order to earn bread, although he suffers from stomach problems, he cannot rest like wealthy people who are used to being pampered; nor is he fortunate enough to be admitted to a hospital; he cannot even raise the money to buy medicine. He only (drags), no mistake, (dragging) is a poor person's helpless but wonderful way of dealing with (sickness)!

However, now he has failed, (dragging) can no longer be effective against the disease demon; even if he wants to live, to earn bread, the evil disease is no longer allowing him to. Although he is very anxious, it is no use, he can only sleep in bed, in a small room of less than ten feet around, with a window hole as small as a dog's kennel, stifling so that he can't breathe!

At this moment, he stared at the ceiling, a slow, slight pain brewing in his stomach, his body running a high fever, his heart longing for the life to come. Poverty and disease intertwined to form a tight net, deeply enveloping him. The raindrops outside the window were still tapping on the window panes, and the ruthless wind continued to blow fiercely.

He has no friends, let alone relatives. He is alone in Shanghai. If he does not work for a day, he will go hungry, so he has no savings. He did not anticipate this sudden illness. Therefore, he has no money to hire a doctor, let alone a way to ward off the disease demon. He can only wait for the natural evolution of the disease!

When he is awake, everything in front of him is very quiet. There are no smiling faces, no hypocritical expressions, no red-headed foreign devils, let alone women's legs; what his eyes come into contact with is only the ceiling, the airtight window panes, and simple utensils. But his ears are busy: the music from the radio, the hawkers' shouts, the urgent sound of ambulance bells, the sound of wind and rain hitting the poor... all of it pounding his eardrums, making him annoyed and impatient! But there is no way out.

He also has moments of confusion, and dreamlike emotions run up his mind: he thinks of his hometown, he thinks of his deceased parents, and even more of his wandering brothers. He seems to have slipped and fallen into a deep abyss, startling him into a cold sweat.

This 丨sweat丨 seems not to be without benefit to him, or perhaps it is because he has been resting for several days, the cold has gradually subsided, the fever has gradually subsided, although his body is still pitifully weak, but for the sake of earning bread, the lonely and unrecovered he, had to drag his weak body again and embark on the journey of struggle.

Customs of Fuzhou: Marriage

Chen Yu

The day before or two days before a woman gets married, she must, as a rule, perform the trick of "abstaining from grains." The purpose of this is nothing more than to prevent her from urinating or defecating in the sedan chair or at the groom's house. If such a thing unfortunately happens, it will not only be impossible to solve, but the groom's family will also consider it an ominous sign; or as a result, their relationship will be discordant and a tragedy will occur. It is truly (unfortunate to be born a daughter)!

The night before the wedding, the daughter and mother both cry (with great joy)! The way of crying is not the way we usually wail loudly when stimulated; nor is it the sobbing and weeping of (shedding tears in secret). It is a small song of (question and answer) that is both crying and not crying: the mother often sings: "Sister, oh sister, when you go to someone else's house, you must listen to the (tangbu)'s mouth, oh sister!" "Listening to the tangbu's mouth means obeying the husband's words." "Mother, oh mother, the daughter is young and does not know etiquette, oh mother!" (In Fuzhou, the mother is usually called (mother). The daughter answers in this way as a rule. If you don't know this custom, listening to this little song is really baffling! When she is about to get married, the mother must first take care of the two procedures of washing her hair and shaving her face for her daughter, and then push her out of the main hall. At this time, the parents sit upright in the hall, and the daughter kneels down on both knees to express her gratitude for the kindness of raising her. At the same time, the two elders must put on her the (veil) (a kind of hat worn by women when they get married), and then she officially gets into the sedan chair. But when she is about to get into the sedan chair, the daughter often acts as if she does not want to go, and is pushed by her family members again and again, as if she is very reluctant to get into the sedan chair.

When the sedan chair starts to move, the family members all see her off with tearful eyes. Only the mother and her daughter in the sedan chair repeat their old tune of last night. At the same time, the mother also holds a lot of melon seeds or wheat and throws them randomly at the top of the sedan chair. This action has two meanings, one (melon seeds) is to express that after the daughter gets married, she will have sons and daughters and her descendants will be numerous; one (wheat) is to express that the daughter will not starve in the future. But at this time, there is a contradictory behavior, that is, as soon as the sedan chair leaves the door, they must block the door, as if if they are a little slower, the so-called (feng shui) will definitely be sucked away by her. Such superstition is really rare.

When the bridal sedan chair is about to arrive at the groom's house, the groom and his father must avoid it. It is said that when the bridal sedan chair enters the door, there is a kind of (killing energy) that specializes in killing them. If they do not avoid it and are hit by it, even if they do not die, they will at least be half dead from illness.

The sedan chair is placed in the hall. At this time, the groom's family must call a child of about seven or eight years old to stand in front of the sedan door and ask her to get out of the sedan chair. With obligation comes natural right, and the bridesmaid (the bride's companion) will give him a package of gifts (usually money) prepared by her in the bride's house to express her gratitude. At this time, the groom has come out, and the so-called grand ceremony of four bows and eight prostrations is carried out at this time. However, the groom must know a little when bowing, that is, do not kneel down on the seventh bow or the last bow to show the meaning of (male superiority to female inferiority). If not, it will inevitably be ridiculed by the guests.

Then the so-called (sitting on the bed) is carried out. What is called (sitting on the bed)? It is the way they point (male left and female right), sitting silently by the bed. At this time, there is a very interesting thing, whether male or female, they all want to pull the other's lapel to sit under their own buttocks. The intention is that in this way, the other party will definitely obey him or her in the future. I remember not long ago, I had a relative whose head was not very clear. When he got married, his friends coaxed him and said (if the bride pulls your lapel to sit on, you must stand up to show your disapproval). He actually did it as he was told, and as a result, the lapel was torn by half a foot.

Modern Celebrity Paintings and Calligraphy

Mr. Diao Qiusheng (Brief History)

Shi Lin, style name Sheng, also known as Changlu, is currently working at the No. 2 New Spinning Factory in Shanghai West. The time spent sitting on the bed is very short, at most about a quarter of an hour. At this time, the bridesmaid calls the groom (to lift the crown) (to pull down the bride's crown), and at the same time calls many guests to appreciate the true colors of the newlyweds. Then the bride changes her clothes, and after changing her clothes, they walk out of the hall and carry out the trick of (knocking on the bamboo pole). The so-called (knocking on the bamboo pole) is that the groom desperately pulls family members or guests and wants them to sit upright in the hall and accept his and her bow. After the bow, they must give a gift. At this time, the guests and family members run east and west (except for parents or grandmother), which is very interesting!

After (knocking on the bamboo pole), they both go to the kitchen to worship the (God of the Kitchen). At this time, no matter how delicate you are, the bride must go to the well or the river to fetch two buckets of water to show that she can take on the responsibility of running the household.

In the evening, the wedding night party starts as usual. The procedure for the party is that the guests stand by the door, knock on the door with their hands, and sing the so-called (wedding door poem). When they sing to a certain extent, the bridesmaid will open the door and let them in. If you can't sing, then don't even think about making a fuss. The ways of making a fuss are probably all about ordering plays, such as (Li Taibai taking off his boots), (Guanyin dripping dew), and so on. If they do not follow the words of the guests at this time, it is to (shame) them and call them to (take back the cage arm) ( (shame) and (take back the cage arm) both mean to lose face), this kind of (shame) and (take back the cage arm) is no small matter, and often as a result, relatives lose their feelings. Therefore, the groom and bride must implement it no matter what. I remember that a friend of mine in the past, when he got married, his relatives wanted to see the bride's navel. The bride was certainly unwilling, but she was afraid that the relationship with her relatives would break down, so she had to cut a hole in the middle of a whole set of new clothes with scissors towards the navel. The guests were of course very happy, but the next day the bride hanged herself. In the 20th century, this kind of bad habit is still left over, which is really (outrageous)?

The wedding night party must last until one or two o'clock in the evening before it can end. After the end, they naturally prepare to sleep. But at this time, the bridesmaid comes out and knocks on the groom's bamboo pole. She takes a square piece of red cloth (called (number one scholar bag) in Fuzhou dialect, used for intercourse that night) and gives it to him, asking him to reward her. No matter what, she refuses to leave, intentionally delaying your precious night. There is also a strange example, that is, at this time, if there is money in the groom's pocket, no matter how much, it will be searched and taken away by her, and he cannot resist.

The next day, the bride's family, as a rule, will send someone to invite them to a (double trip) (inviting a double trip means inviting them to go to the bride's house together), but it cannot be overnight, no matter how far the journey is. They all have to come back. After that, there are still (inviting for three days), (inviting for ten days), (inviting for a full month), etc., inviting them with great joy! However, most of the invitations are for single trips, and the groom usually does not participate, so they are both unwilling, but the custom is like this, and they have to do it. It is really pitiful!

Resignation

Wei Fan has decided to leave. In the small room where he lived, there was only a table, a chair, and a bed facing the door. Today, everything in the room has been tidied up by him. The setting sun reflects back from the opposite wall, making it even more refreshing. There is nothing on the table, and it is very clean. Two boxes and a well-tied bedding are placed flat in front of the bed. There is only a tattered empty tent left on the bed. He sits leaning on the chair, his eyes staring straight at the luggage that is already prepared and placed in front of the bed, motionless, envisioning the fate and situation he will encounter after leaving his job. Suddenly, he stands up, his feelings seem to be more determined, stomps his foot, and mumbles:

Page 19

Yes, Wei Fan's profession has made him too unsatisfied. He has been working at the T Factory in C Port for a full four years. He was not very satisfied when he first came with a monthly salary of eight yuan, and it has not increased at all until now. Moreover, recently the manager of T Factory, on the pretext of poor business, issued a notice of (paying wages at 80% off). How could he bear it? After a long period of deliberation, Wei Fan decided not to continue his current job.

(What am I doing? Am I spacing out? I ran out from thousands of miles away for a job with no hope for the future and a monthly salary of a few dollars? ... I'm not doing it! Resign! To hell with it!) He wrote a letter to his uncle in Shanghai, who had introduced him before, explaining his distress that he had to resign, and asked him to find another way for him as much as possible, but he did not dare to resign, so he asked the manager for four weeks' leave, preparing to see his uncle.

Now he is all prepared. He will rest in the room for a while, and wait for the boat to Shanghai tonight to leave the place where he has been for less than four years.

The journey was very peaceful. On the evening of the second day, Wei Fan found himself in the living room of his uncle's house. He met his uncle. He reiterated his previous intention in a tactful manner, with dry lips and tongue, and explained in detail the reasons why he had to resign and the hopeless situation for the future. As a result, his uncle, in addition to telling him that industry and commerce were declining and there was a surplus of people with no other way to think about, also told him decisively to return to the factory when his leave was over.

(Yes, there is no way! Industry and commerce are declining, and there is a surplus of people. What way can I think about?) Wei Fan carefully tasted his uncle's threatening words, and at the same time thought: (Unless I go home and eat old rice, but what about the criticisms of relatives and the situation of the family? What should I do?)

X X X X

One evening four weeks later, Wei Fan's slender shadow was repeatedly reflected on the wall of his small room in the T Factory.

Odds and Ends: Xian Yu

(1) To be a modern leader, in addition to his excellent knowledge, his fists must be bigger than others.

(2) (Darkness will always be overcome by light). People say this. But when will this (future) (will) come, no one knows.

(6) An artist's room is like a fortune-telling stall.

(7) Human friendship and hatred are both transferred by interests.

(8) The current world, in addition to only having power and no justice, is also a world that only allows modern women to enjoy pleasure and does not allow the survival of country girls.

(9) Ideal things often end up being contradictory.

(10) A wedding invitation of knocking on the bamboo pole type, although it is decorated with words such as (honored to be loved, dare to inform you), in fact it is (the invitation goes and the gift comes).

(11) (Possession) is human instinct, and (jealousy) is an innate emotion.

(12) The walls of streets and alleys are vents for the weak. No matter how you write, people will just glance at them.

(14) If we can collect all the kinds of exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous taxes collected in various places in our country, we can compile a (Directory of Hundred Taxes).

(15) A person who is gloomy and does not talk idly is definitely not a good thing.

Drama

War and Peace (II) (7) (A Play in Four Acts) Ling

Act Three: Ode to Peace

Time: Twenty-second day of the same month of the returning year.

Location: A certain official residence in Beiping.

Characters:

A Military Authority, around 40 years old.

A Political Authority, around 50 years old.

Six or seven Newspaper Reporters, of varying ages, all male.

Military Officer's Wife, around 25 or 26 years old.

Military Officer's Young Master, around 13 years old.

A Stable Boy, around 22 years old.

Small Mine Owner (Westerner), around 40 years old.

A Financial Tycoon, around 40 years old.

President of the Chamber of Commerce, under 50.

Second Secretary of the Embassy (Japanese), around 30 years old.

Confidential Secretary, around 20 years old.

University President, around 40 years old.

Peace Delegate, under 35 years old.

Maid, around 19 years old.

Setting: A section of a large Western-style house. The stage is about two and a half, with a large, ornate living room on the right. A staircase at the back leads to the upstairs bedrooms. Next to the staircase hangs a velvet curtain, leading to the inner living room. A door on the right wall leads to the corridor. There is also a door on the left wall, leading to other rooms in the house. The left is a protruding part. Vines climb the walls. There is a window on the far left. Above is a balcony on the second floor.

When the curtain opens, the stage is empty. The entire stage is diffused with a soft glow. The room is filled with an atmosphere of peace.

The balcony and walls on the left still reflect intense sunlight. Soon, the Military Authority pulls aside the velvet curtain and comes out of the living room, walking towards the stairs. Behind him follows the young Confidential Secretary, carrying a briefcase, as he is about to go out on important business.

Military Authority: Go take a trip. The main thing is to find out what his opinion is.

Confidential Secretary: Yes. (Goes straight to the door on the right of the stage and exits. The Military Authority also slowly walks up the stairs. The intoxicating sound of a record playing can be heard. Soon after, the Maid exits from the door next to the staircase on the left wall, clearing away teacups and fruit platters. She is followed by the Stable Boy, cracking melon seeds.)

Maid: How about it? Young Master! Call me "Big Sister" and I'll give you an American orange to eat.

Stable Boy: Big Sister!

Maid: Oh! What a good little brother. (Throws him an orange.) You have to be more obedient in the future!

Stable Boy: Oh! Look! You're really putting on airs now. When have I ever not listened to you? Is there even a need to say it?

Maid: Hmph, still arguing. Last night I told you not to run to my room, but why did you sneak in again? Is that what you call listening?

Stable Boy: Now that I've eaten an orange, I'll be obedient.

Maid: Stop talking nonsense. I'm asking you, if the Japanese soldiers really invade, what do you plan to do? Our Madam is really anxious.

Stable Boy: What's so hard about that? I'm only afraid they won't invade.

Maid: Why?

Stable Boy: Isn't it obvious? If they really invade, then everyone will flee. The Master and Madam will flee, and we will flee too. If they're not careful, we can slip away privately and live a good life. Don't you think that's great?

Maid: Oh my, you make it sound so good. There isn't a single man we can rely on.

Stable Boy: Can't you rely on me? You just watch. If I, Little Wang, say it, I'll do it. I'm just afraid the Japanese soldiers won't invade, then there's no way to do it.

Maid: Yes, it seems you're just a coward. It looks like we have to make a vow before the Bodhisattva, hoping the Japanese soldiers will come so we can run, otherwise we'll be stuck being servants here for life. Is that it?

Film Special

Clark Gable Seriously Ill

— Hel

Exposure to Cold and Dampness While Hunting Causes Lung Problems - Return to Hollywood, Appendicitis Flare-Up

Clark Gable, once celebrated as the epitome of masculinity, is now seriously ill. American film magazines are full of reports of his condition. One magazine said, "While we cannot say that Clark Gable will never return to the screen, we have investigated and determined that if he is to return, it will be at least several months, certainly not a few weeks, before he can be expected to recover. The studio is very anxious for him to recover quickly and is promoting the story that he refused to co-star with Joan Crawford in 'No Woman Wanted' because he didn't like the script, using his illness as an excuse. In reality, Clark Gable's illness is not an excuse, but a genuine illness, and a very serious one at that."

Clark Gable's illness was caused by his recent hunting trip. He is extremely fond of outdoor sports. Whenever he had a vacation or a break from filming, he would invite many friends to go hunting or fishing in the mountains. However, in the past, many people would go with him, including both men and women, and Clark's wife would always participate. Because his wife and other women were with him, Clark always felt that he wasn't having as much fun. He said, "One day, I'll take a good friend and go hunting, and really enjoy myself. I hate it when women follow behind and tell men 'Be careful!' 'That gully is too dangerous, don't go!' or 'That peak is too steep, don't go!' 'Don't get your shoes wet!' as if men were three-year-old children." So this time, Clark Gable only invited Dr. Dolph to go with him.

They had a great time for the first few days. No one told them not to do this or not to do that, and no one was watching them. They really went where they wanted to go and did what they wanted to do, completely uninhibited. Sometimes, they weren't ready to return to their tents until late at night, their hunting enthusiasm still unspent. As for whether their socks were wet or not, and all the other nagging they usually heard, they would think about it and laugh.

One day, they returned extremely exhausted. They had suffered so much hardship and encountered so much danger in one day, and they had also waded through several rivers. They returned to their tent soaked in water and sweat, wanting to change clothes. But they were too tired, so they lay down on the bed and fell asleep. They slept for several hours. When they woke up, it was late at night, and the weather was cold. They felt cold and damp all over. Of course, they didn't care about a little cold or a little cough. But the little cold and little cough got deeper and deeper, and it was clear that the cold air had entered their lungs. By the time morning came, they couldn't continue hunting. So they decided to return to Hollywood, get their bodies healthy, and then continue their fun.

The doctor was fine, but when Clark Gable arrived in Hollywood, he had several sore spots on his back. He lay in bed, and the pain gradually moved downwards. By the next day, both of his feet were so painful that he couldn't move them. The studio didn't know about his condition and sent someone to ask him to continue filming the almost-completed "Hold Your Man." Clark Gable immediately put the public interest first, gritted his teeth, and endured the pain to film the few remaining scenes in one go. The camera was rolling, and Clark was struggling. When the filming was over, he collapsed. He was taken home in an ambulance.

So they quickly called in specialists and used X-rays to examine all parts of his body. The result was that he was diagnosed with typhoid fever and other ailments, as well as a sudden attack of appendicitis. But with his condition like this, they couldn't possibly operate on him again. Since news of his condition spread, the entire Hollywood community has been shaken. Many people are praying for him to recover quickly. But this is not an illness from which he can recover in a few weeks. It will be at least several months or half a year before he can return to the film set.

Film Reviews

Review of "The Penguin Pool Murder"

— Ling He

Almost every detective film is the same. The main thing is to use the trick of adults deceiving children, interweaving the plot in a bizarre and tortuous way, filled with doubt, so that the audience watches with bated breath to find out who the murderer is.

This RKO Pictures production, "The Penguin Pool Murder," is the same. First, it raises suspicions of rape and murder, then a corpse is discovered, and then the police arrest several suspects. Then, thanks to the clever research of a detective and a female teacher, clues are slowly found. Unfortunately, just when the case is about to be solved, the witness is brutally murdered. In the end, thanks to the female teacher's clever plan, the truth is revealed: the murderer is the lawyer defending the accused.

I remember Paramount's "The Benson Murder Case" was largely the same, with the detective as the murderer, using his talent and eloquence to incriminate the innocent. The similarity is that the lawyer or detective, who is supposed to protect civil rights, is actually the murderer.

In this respect, it is a manifestation of the contradictions of modern society. If the author's intention is to expose this, then it is undoubtedly worthy of praise. However, we believe that the author wrote the script in this way simply to make the plot more bizarre and novel, in an attempt to win the audience's applause. Because of this, the detective and the lawyer are inevitably used as sources of ridicule.

However, on the other hand, perhaps the author wanted to use this play to offer sincere advice to those responsible for society, hoping to improve this contradictory phenomenon. However, in "The Penguin Pool Murder," the point of earnest advice is not emphasized, which can be said to be very weak. Moreover, this is a fundamental contradiction in modern society and cannot be eliminated with a few soft words. Therefore, the author's efforts are ultimately unrewarding.

As mentioned above, this film is quite well-equipped with the main conditions for a detective film. But overall, the director's handling of the plot is really not powerful. So much dialogue, that to American audiences it would allow them to close their eyes and listen as if it was Radio, but to Chinese audiences, they can only doze off in the theater. In addition, the so-called tension, apart from the strange bird sounds at night and the moment in court, is all very forced and loses the effect of tension.

The author used Edna May Oliver and James Gleason as the protagonists, naturally wanting to use their awkward faces to make the plot lively. But unfortunately, due to the script's decision, they couldn't enliven it. We believe that none of the characters here is worthy of special praise, and the director's technique is just as mediocre overall.

Finally, we want to talk about the social basis for producing detective films.

Since modern society is so corrupt, it is an undeniable fact. There is no possibility of boasting and embellishment, and it is unbearable to expose ugliness. So, on the one hand, there are some farmer-consciousness martial arts works, and at the same time, the so-called detective films can allow the audience to unconsciously spend some extra time. If this is used to show the progress of science and use science to solve bizarre cases, then science is just used as an ornament on the screen.

Audience Opinions

After Seeing "Man Jiang Hong"

— Qiran

Forcing a very long classical novel into a film script, naturally, there is danger of failure everywhere. However, this adaptation of "Man Jiang Hong," though still inevitably a bit stiff and forced in places, unexpectedly achieved considerable success. This, I think, is perhaps the result of the efforts of the script editors and directors.

We all know that the lifeline of old novels largely depends on the word "fate" in "(those who are destined will meet even from a thousand miles away)". Since ancient times, the meeting of talented scholars and beautiful women has been because their "fate" contains "fate". After meeting, they are bound to fall in love at first sight. This "Man Jiang Hong" is a classical novel, so it cannot be an exception to this point. Like the relationship between Shui Cun and Tao Zhi, there is "fate" at play everywhere. Because there is too much "fate", it becomes coincidence. Too many coincidences cause a loss of truthfulness, and the power of a work that loses truthfulness becomes weak.

What era is this! In this era, everyone is shouting that movies should enlighten the way out for those who have gone astray. To what extent does "Man Jiang Hong" achieve this? Does it enlighten the way out for those who have gone astray? No, it only depicts the laziness, idleness, weakness, and fear of the petty bourgeoisie. Although it intentionally and reluctantly makes Shui Cun realize at the end, in the end he still cannot help but drown in anguish and die!

Cheng Bugao is much more progressive here than in "Raging Torrent." That kind of cheerful and gentle tone added a lot of interest to the audience. The fact that he can keep the audience sitting for two hours without getting bored is indeed a rare thing.

The Adaptation of "Man Jiang Hong"

— Lin Ding

(Omitted above) Here I would like to talk about some issues of adapting the original book with Mr. Wang Qianbai, the adapter of the screenplay. It is undeniable that if an audience member read the original novel, will almost suspect that the Man Jiang Hong seen on the silver screen is another similar story. Of course, trying to move four thick volumes of a novel to a few thousand feet of film is indeed a difficult task. However, since we already know the difficulty, we should not ignore the essence of the original book. For example: the name of the original book is "Man Jiang Hong," and the main point is the "Man Jiang Hong" performed in the dance troupe, leading to the ending of the ship fire, in order to take care of the original meaning of the book's title. But in the Man Jiang Hong on the silver screen, it almost makes people feel that it is somewhat off-topic. I believe that the editor should have inserted this, even if it meant shortening some of the interactions between Wan Youguang and Tao Zhi. Because the capitalists' playing with women can be clearly understood by the audience from the positions of Wan Youguang and Tao Zhi, and since this is for the sake of economy on the film, it would be more appropriate to sacrifice this. There was no consciousness at all in the original book, but the adapter could not bear to give up the original subject matter and also wanted to infuse some new consciousness, resulting in the entire "Man Jiang Hong" play being scattered and unbearable. For example, Tao Zhi on the silver screen struggled out of the hands of the capitalists, and died in the arms of her lover. Although this is more powerful than Tao Zhi's drowning and death in the original book, it also tells a person that when there is no way to deal with reality, there is only confused sinking, and it also implies that the power of the capitalists is impossible to deal with! The original "Man Jiang Hong" could only be supplied for entertainment, and there was no possibility of adapting it into a screenplay. Here we can understand how difficult it is to adapt a screenplay, especially when you want to change an old subject matter and give it a new consciousness. It is unrewarding and easy to make mistakes. I wonder if Mr. Wang also feels sympathy for this?

Talking About "Flying Catkins"

— Zhuo Qun

(Omitted above) Strictly speaking: the biggest regret in the performance of "Flying Catkins" is because it is restricted by the script and lacks dramatic "force". After watching this film, the impression is like reading a poem. Fortunately, the director worked very hard here and arranged such a story very meticulously. Moreover, the performance skills of each part also show the director's experience and familiarity from time to time. However, the entire plot is loose, and I always feel that it cannot tightly grasp the heartstrings of the audience. Instead, the subtitles gave a lot of help to the whole drama. There are several joints where the dramatic power is insufficient, and all of them rely on powerful explanations to weave and arrange them. So, in terms of the formation of the whole film, it is not too annoying.

In terms of performance, Yuan Meiyun is still the most successful one. The innocence and activity of the cattle-herding period; the abuse suffered during the servant period and the adoptive daughter-in-law period, and the cruelty given by the world, each performance is deeply moving and can arouse the sympathy of the audience. Wang Huijuan plays a gentle and incompetent woman, and her performance has improved compared to "Little Actress". Bao Zhichao's acting is too stiff. The rest, such as Tian Fang, Wu Yixiao, Chen Qixia, and Cang Yinqiu, are all mediocre. The scenery is still realistic, and the lighting in some places in the photography is too dark, but there is no major problem. To sum up in one sentence: the performance of "Flying Catkins" seems to lack dramatic (ness), but because (work) has considerable success, it is (worth seeing).

Film Novel

Trinkets (7)

— Cong Mei

Yuan Pu stood up to say goodbye. Auntie Ye helped him straighten his tie and took him to the door. He said, "I might not see you again for seven or eight years. The last thing I want to say is... because I am a person, I should fulfill my obligations to the country... But, at the same time, because I have a heart, I will always love you!"

Auntie Ye stood still in a daze, smiling, but tears were surging in her eyes. Yuan Pu was gone; he had left bravely. She leaned against the door, tears streaming down her face, all alone, even more desolate!

Undoubtedly, Auntie Ye was stimulated. She retreated into the house, her steps light and weak, her spirit drooping. As she sat down, the bitter tears in her eyes rolled out like pearls. "Why does everyone have to have a heart?" she asked miserably, pointing to her own heart.

Zhu'er came in and saw her mother crying, so she threw herself into her arms and told her not to cry. "Mom!... Only silly people cry!" Zhu'er used her little finger to catch her mother's tears and flicked them towards the mud monk, and then they both laughed.

◆◆◆◆

In the vast darkness of night, a train was traveling in the distance. Yuan Pu was rushing from the darkness to his bright future! At this time, in a dilapidated house where the last lamp had not yet been extinguished, there was silence. Old Ye was snoring like a dead pig. Yu'er was smiling in her sleep. Zhu'er clung tightly to her mother's embrace. As for Auntie Ye? She had her eyes wide open, unable to sleep in the middle of the night. She stared at the ceiling in a daze, as if she heard the sound of the rumbling wheels; as if she saw Yuan Pu's shadow. Her heart was disturbed. She could only secretly shed tears in the silent air!

Spring came again, another year. At that moment of dawn, the lake and mountains were still so beautiful. But the warm spring breeze could not reach the home of Old Ye, who was becoming increasingly impoverished. Everything had changed! Old Ye was wearing ragged clothes, and he was also sick, coughing and panting, looking even more pitiful!

"Zhu'er's father! Was that you coughing just now?... Auntie Ye asked when she heard the coughing, concerned that his illness had flared up again.

"No!... I've been much better lately!" he said, putting on a smile. Auntie Ye was drowsy; but her soul was being invaded by grief! (To be continued)
